Qingdao Naval and Army Forces Suppress Jiaozhou Bandits

Qingdao dispatch: A large group of bandits was recently discovered in the area of the Greater and Lesser Zhushan Mountains west of Jiaozhou Bay. The Qingdao Public Security Bureau dispatched police along with the Yongxiang warship of the navy to suppress them. The bandits fled upon hearing the news. When the military police departed and returned to Qingdao, they reappeared and harassed Xuejiadao and other places. The Qingdao authorities, believing that the bandits were so rampant that they could not pacify the maritime frontier without severely suppressing them, dispatched Fang Lianbi, the captain of the Security Brigade, with two security teams and two mortars from the municipal government on the 21st. The Northeast Navy dispatched two companies of naval infantry, as well as the Zhenhai and Yongxiang warships, and also dispatched two aircraft to fly to Jiaozhou Bay to scout and assist. At noon that day, the naval and army police arrived at Xuejiadao on the Feijing ship and camped at Lingshanwei that evening. Upon hearing the news, the bandits fled into the Panlong Temple in the Lesser Zhushan Mountains to observe the situation. The military police immediately tracked them forward and notified the Jiaoxian County government to dispatch a team to suppress them. At the same time, they contacted the local militia and ordered them to guide them forward. Yesterday, the Naval Headquarters received a telegram from the captain of the Yongxiang warship stating that the bandits intended to enter the sea from Chejialing and escape. It requested that the Haihe warship be sent to Huangdao to intercept them. The navy has now dispatched a warship to go there. (April 23)

Recent News of Communist Bandits Wreaking Havoc in Guangdong and Guangxi

Guangzhou dispatch: The Communist bandits in northern Guangdong, after withdrawing from Nanxiong and Shixing, regrouped in southern Jiangxi and recaptured Xinfeng. The Guangdong army, based on reports that a force led by Zhu and Peng was still lingering in the Yu Ling Mountains, fearing that they would re-enter the Guangdong border from Yu Ling, has recently been conducting anti-bandit operations in northern Guangdong with unusual caution. At present, no fewer than 8,000 troops are gathered between Shaozhou and Shixing. The 3rd Battalion of Wu Wenxian's regiment, led by He Ding, is stationed in Mashi, Shixing. Chen Hanguang's regiment is stationed at the Hedong and Haba train stations opposite Shaoguan. Liang Gongfu's battalion of Zeng Youren's regiment is stationed in Shixing County. Two battalions are stationed in Zhou Tian, Renhua. The remaining teams, totaling about 7,000 people, are preparing to enter Nanxiong and join Zhang Huizan's division in Ganzhou to suppress the Xinfeng force. At the same time, troops are dispatched diagonally to the northeast to guard Longnan, preventing the Communist bandits from disturbing Lianping and Xingning in northeastern Guangdong after abandoning Xinfeng. The various armies in northern Guangdong are currently under the command of Wu Wenxian. At the same time, the provincial government has repeatedly received reports that the hidden Communist bandits in eastern Guangdong are planning to make trouble again, intending to collude with the Zhu and Peng force on the Jiangxi border to attack Lianping and Xingning. It has urgently telegraphed Dai Ji's 8th Brigade of the Eastern Guangdong Defense Army to quickly dispatch large detachments to defend Lianping, Heping, and Xinfeng and to coordinate with Wu Wenxian's troops in northern Guangdong to strictly prevent the Communist bandits from suddenly invading. At the same time, it ordered the county magistrates of various counties to quickly reorganize the militia to assist the military police in assuming responsibility for local security. As for the organization of the security team, it is currently urgently recruiting strong men. If the number of people in the four major teams cannot be fully recruited, two major teams will be established first. As for Guangxi, because the war is still undecided, both sides are stationed with heavy troops in Guiping and Guixian, and they are currently in a stalemate. Therefore, the military strength in the interior of Guangxi Province is extremely empty. Previously, Longzhou was raided by a large group of Communist bandits led by Yu Zuoyu and others. After Yu was severely suppressed by Yang Tenghui's troops of the Guangxi army, Yu began to flee east. According to a businessman who returned to Guangdong from Guangxi, the Communist bandits Yu Zuoyu and Wei Baqun once spied on Baise in the middle of this month but were repelled by Yang Tenghui's troops and fled back to the Fengshan Donglan area. After a brief stay, they learned that the defense forces of Liuzhou Qianjiang Binyang had all been transferred to Xun Gui for combat. Qingyuan and Liuzhou were empty. Yu and Wei then invaded Qing Liu from Donglan, inciting two or three thousand local bandits along the way, declaring that they would occupy Qing Liu as a base. Wherever they passed, houses were burned, and gentlemen and wealthy people were slaughtered. Recently, Yishan, Nandan, and Hechi counties have been devastated, and Liuzhou has been shaken. Li Zongren and Huang Shaoxiong were unable to return to suppress the rebellion because the team had set out to Dahe. They are still transferring Yang Tenghui's troops from Nanning via Qianjiang to Liuzhou to suppress them. (April 21)

Sino-Russian Conference

Notification to the Russian Side Has Been Answered

Preparatory Office for Sino-Russian Conference Established

Mo Dehui Prepares to Depart for Russia

The Scope of the Meeting Still Follows the Declaration on Russia

Harbin dispatch, 19th: The notification to Russia to convene a meeting, which was sent out many days ago, was answered by the Russian side at noon today. Today, the Russian Consul-General in Harbin, Melnikov, called Zhong Yu of the Special Envoy's Office at around 9:00 AM. At that time, Zhong was working at the Municipal Preparatory Office outside Daowai and had not yet arrived. The staff inside the office urgently called on his behalf. Zhong immediately came to the office and also called the Russian consulate, which was answered by the Russian consul. He said that he had just received instructions from his government to be responsible for the reply. Moscow has received the notice from China to send representatives to the meeting. The special envoy is prepared to receive the Harbin Russian Consulate. The consulate will not be open for three days for the Memorial Day holiday. After resuming work next Tuesday, it will send a formal reply. Zhong immediately informed Mo Dehui and telegraphed the central and northeast authorities separately. All matters concerning Mo's departure abroad are currently being actively prepared. A Sino-Russian Conference Preparatory Office has been established in the office of the Director-General of the Chinese Eastern Railway, and Secretary-General Cai Yunchun has been appointed as the director of the office. It is divided into two sections, accounting and general affairs, which are handled by Feng Jie, the secretary of the Railway Council, and Sun Wendou, the consul of Shuangchengpu, who will accompany him to Russia. Yesterday, travel expenses were issued to the entourage. Other professionals have not yet been sought for compromise. Li Shaogeng and Wang Zupei will not be going due to other matters. Cui Shuyan and Feng Jie, two female Russian secretaries from the Railway Council, will accompany them. The travel expenses from the central government have not yet been allocated. Mo has asked Liaoning to pay in advance. The estimated travel time is 20 days, and the meeting will last for one and a half months. In his spare time, he will travel to France and Germany to investigate their transportation and road conditions. After Mo's departure, the Office of the Director-General of the Chinese Eastern Railway will set up an office and appoint a commissioner to be responsible for handling matters related to domestic liaison. The scope of the meeting will still follow the Central Declaration on Russia as the outline, and no other matters will be discussed. Although Russia has expressed its desire to expand the scope of negotiations, our side has not accepted it. Various external rumors are not credible.

Liang Zhongjia's Coffin Arrives in Harbin

More than 10,000 People Greeted and Mourned at the Station

Received Mourning from the People Along the Way

Harbin dispatch, 19th: After the death of Mr. Liang Zhongjia, funeral services were held in Hailar on the 13th, 14th, and 15th. Representatives from various institutions and people's organizations in the Northeast attended the funeral. On the morning of the 17th of this month, the coffin was transported from Hailar to Harbin. Liang Zuozhou (Liang Zhongjia's uncle) first came to this port to notify acquaintances and friends, and the funeral preparation office at Liang's residence sent letters to all sectors, stating that it would arrive in Harbin at 10:00 AM on the 19th. On that day, starting from 9:00 AM, more than 10,000 people from various institutions and the public arrived at the station to greet and mourn the coffin. The platform was extremely crowded both inside and outside. Later, the funeral office at Liang's residence distributed yellow and blue paper flowers to the mourners to show some restrictions. Important figures such as Zhang Jinghui, the chief executive of the Special District, Mo Dehui, the director-general of the Chinese Eastern Railway, He Yufang, the mayor, and Bao Wenying, the chief of the Special Police Department, all arrived. A large detachment of military police arrived, and many monks and Taoists also arrived. More than 60 monks from the Jile Temple automatically participated in chanting scriptures. At 10:05 AM, the hearse entered the station, with a combined passenger and freight car. When the door of the hearse opened, mourning music played loudly. Zhang Jinghui led all sectors to set up a memorial service on the platform and read the eulogy. At around 11:00 AM, the coffin was carried out of the station. The coffin was made of fir wood and covered with red silk. The outer coffin was purchased and donated by Wan Fulin, the chairman of the Black Province. After being placed on a dragon-head and phoenix-tail sedan chair, it was carried by sixty-four people. The ceremonial guard in front stretched for several miles, passing through the station street, turning into Lama Terrace, turning into Dazhi Street, and heading to Jile Temple. A large detachment of military police was assigned to escort the coffin, and many dignitaries also walked there. Along the streets, crowds stood to watch. Everyone took off their hats to pay their respects as the coffin passed. Zhang Xueliang sent Deputy Officer Chen as his representative to set up a shrine on Dazhi Street and greet the coffin. At 12:30 PM, the coffin arrived at Jile Temple and was placed in the mourning hall. The escorts lit incense, offered wine, paid their respects, and dispersed. From the 19th to the 21st, Zhang Jinghui funded the construction of a shed in the mourning hall to chant scriptures for three days and decided to lead his subordinates and all sectors of society in a public memorial service on the 20th. When the coffin was transported from Hailar, it was delayed for two days due to the people welcoming and mourning along the way before it arrived in Harbin. The citizens of Hailar organized a memorial meeting and divided it into propaganda, documents, and other departments to handle affairs. Many slogans were posted on the hearse, and declarations were issued at the stations along the way, describing Liang's integrity and achievements. Wang Erzhan, the chief of staff of the Hulunbuir Garrison Command, Liu Bin, the chief of staff of the 15th Brigade, and Zhao Zhongren, the director of the Hulunbuir Municipal Preparatory Office, accompanied the coffin. The Heilongjiang Provincial Government sent Dou Lianfang, the director of the Public Security Bureau, and Kang Du, two councilors, to Harbin in advance to handle the transportation procedures. It is reported that Liang's coffin was originally intended to be buried in Hailun, Donghai, Heilongjiang, but is currently temporarily placed in the mourning hall of Jile Temple in Harbin.

Chinese Eastern Railway

The Case of Using Chinese and Russian Languages Concurrently for Telegraph Rights

The Russian Side Submits a Memorandum on Telegraph Rights

Director Hua Opposes the Establishment of a Translation Office

Harbin dispatch, 19th: Yesterday afternoon, the Chinese Eastern Railway Council convened a meeting. Chinese and Russian directors attended the meeting as scheduled. Seventeen ordinary proposals were completely passed. The telegraph rights item was discussed for a long time. The Russian side submitted a memorandum, the content of which roughly stated (before a new contract related to the Chinese Eastern Railway's telegraph rights is officially signed, the telegraph rights contract signed on November 22, 1922, shall be temporarily cited to handle all matters. The Chinese and Russian telegraph authorities must absolutely abide by this contract. After the new contract is established, the Chinese Eastern Railway telegraph office will not accept commercial telegrams and all private telegrams at all places along the Chinese Eastern Railway where there are Chinese telegraph bureaus. When the Chinese telegraph authority deems it necessary, long-distance telephones at all stations along the Chinese Eastern Railway can also be provided for private use. Telegrams sent from the Eastern Province to Russia or from Russia to the Eastern Province shall be sent and received in both Chinese and Russian languages. If the Chinese telegraph bureau needs to transfer lines through the Chinese Eastern Railway telegraph office, it can charge a handling fee according to the lowest value stipulated in the contract. Telegrams sent from the Eastern Province to Russia will still be charged at the current price, that is, 22 gold kopecks (copper coins) for each ordinary telegram sentence and 66 gold kopecks for urgent telegrams. The Chinese Eastern Railway authority shall implement the regulations in the contract regarding the receiving and dispatching of commercial telegrams. The exchange of telegraph handling fees shall be settled every three months). This is very different from the opinions of the Communications Committee and the eight compromise measures proposed by Mo Dehui. Therefore, the original proposal was retained and moved to next week's meeting for discussion.

Regarding the case of using Chinese and Russian languages concurrently in the Chinese Eastern Railway, the Council ordered the Road Bureau to organize a committee to review it, but it has not yet replied. On the 17th of this month, the Russian Bureau Director Rudyi suddenly issued a bureau order to establish a translation office, which is divided into four departments. The translation department formerly attached to the General Affairs Office was merged into it. All translation staff in various departments will also serve in the translation office. However, the bureau order only stated that all Chinese documents would be translated into Russian and did not mention the translation of Russian into Chinese. The Chinese department heads believed that if Chinese was translated into Russian, then the files of each department would be in Russian in the future, which would be very inconvenient for inspection. After the translations of each department were consolidated, the Chinese department heads, many of whom did not know Russian, would have even more difficulties when they obtained Russian documents. Yesterday, the Chinese department heads jointly met with Mo Dehui, the director-general, to express their opinions and oppose this method. The Legal Department of the Road Bureau even sent an official letter to the General Affairs Office, stating the advantages and disadvantages of the matter. The original letter is as follows (replying directly: I have received your letter and respectfully learned that our department's opinion on the establishment of the translation office is as follows: (1) The interpretation of using Chinese and Russian languages concurrently refers to having the same effect. For example, when two countries conclude a treaty and prepare the original in foreign language and Chinese, this is the meaning of concurrent use. The fundamental problem lies in the official document format. If there is a Russian document, a Chinese document must be attached in conjunction, so that it can be called concurrent use. It does not matter whether the translation office exists or not, and it is not a problem. Our department believes that the problem of concurrent use should have another abstract solution. Each department head should provide a written opinion for public discussion in preparation. The dispute cannot be resolved by the existence or non-existence of the translation office. (2) The Chinese Eastern Railway is a joint venture between two countries, and equal employment is an immutable principle. There are many benefits to the concurrent use of languages. For example, when writing to the court, Russian alone cannot be used, and Chinese and Russian must be used concurrently. This can prove that the concurrent use of Chinese and Russian is beneficial to the people. It is not a proper way to use Russian exclusively in the department's official documents. Changing to the concurrent use of Chinese and Russian will benefit both Chinese and foreigners. If the thorough reform is not carried out, the goal of friendship between the two countries will be difficult to achieve. Moreover, each department has its own habits. If Chinese and Russian are used concurrently, it should be discussed in detail with each department. Setting up a translation office will inevitably be arbitrary and all-inclusive, which will not only be useless but will also hinder the process of using Chinese and Russian languages concurrently. Moreover, the Road Bureau has an old translation office and a Chinese-Russian secretariat. If another translation office is set up, there will be organizational conflicts and the suspicion of adding redundant agencies. Tracing back to the meaning of the Council's advocacy of the concurrent use of Chinese and Russian languages, it lies in the concurrent use of spirit and form. For example, the use of Chinese and Russian languages in both internal and external affairs, regardless of the territory, is the form of concurrent use. Being able to combine this form and use public documents consistently in each department is the spirit of concurrent use. The so-called equal effect of languages is nothing more than this. If you plan to set up redundant agencies to manipulate, it is a policy of non-sincere concurrent use of Chinese and Russian languages. Based on the opinions on the right, please advocate the cancellation of the organization of the translation office to avoid affecting the process of using Chinese and Russian documents.) The Council will also discuss this matter at a meeting next week.

After Huoshan County in central Anhui was captured by bandits, Taihu County was also occupied by bandits yesterday. Hangzhou Quick Dispatch

The price of rice in Hangzhou City rose again by 40 cents yesterday (the 24th), with the top-quality rice selling for 16 yuan and 60 cents per stone. The price of cheap rice still sells for 13 yuan and 60 cents per stone. Today, a local rose-tip brand has been added, priced at 17 yuan per stone. The so-called cheap rice of 13 yuan per stone is limited to one斗 per person, but each store has empty baskets, and even buying two or three升 is refused.

The Hangzhou General Chamber of Commerce, together with the Relief Association, sent personnel to Shanghai to purchase cheap rice (Saigon), and more than 4,700 bags have been shipped successively. There are still more than 3,000 bags in preparation for continued shipment. At present, the number of cheap rice needed in each county is very large, and it was decided yesterday to continue to handle 13,000 bags to provide a steady supply.

The detective team of the Provincial Public Security Bureau, together with the 6th Precinct of the Changqingsi District, arrested 18 suspected bandits at the Xinkai Alley Water Bamboo Residence and the Hangzhou Cinema at around 10:00 PM last night, including Qiu Xing Shun, Liang Ri Sheng, Chen Lu Sheng, Qiu Gou Lang, Liang Xiang Qiao, Li Qing Hu, Qian Yi Chen, Zhu Zhen Zhao, Han Xin Lin, Chen Bing Tai, Jin Xian Gao, Zhang Fu Jin, Ke Gao Zeng, Gao Xi Lin, Qiu Qi Lao, Xie Hu Ting, Zhang Ben Gen, and the owner of the Water Bamboo Residence, Qiu Qi Jin, all from Sheng County. After a brief interrogation by Officer Huang, they were transferred to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

The amount of silk donation in Hangzhou has been repeatedly increased, and silk merchants are overwhelmed. Requests for appropriate reductions have been ineffective. Now that the deadline for recognition is approaching again, 12 silk weaving factories, including Hulin, have submitted more than 10 kinds of refined silk fabrics to various party and government agencies, requesting exclusive patent exemptions for a period of 10 years. If approved, the silk donation will be reduced without being reduced.

Local News

Jiading

Rice Merchant Encountered Bandits but Escaped Robbery: Zhang Chunxiang, a rice merchant from Pudong, has been buying and selling grain at various rice shops in Anting Huangdu for a long time. He has a good reputation, so after the transaction is completed, he must wait until he sells out in Shanghai before paying the price. The day before yesterday (the 23rd), he received more than 1,000 yuan of rice money in Shanghai. Because he was in partnership with Mr. Huang of a certain rice shop, they agreed to meet at the station. He took the Shanghai Changzhou train to Huang and got off. After a few words of conversation, the partner took a rickshaw back to the town, and Zhang went to Caijiaqiao, three miles away from the station, to buy goods. At that time, the sky was dim and about to rain, and there were few pedestrians on the road. Unexpectedly, next to the ancient tomb and the thick trees, two bandits wearing black clothes and holding murder weapons suddenly appeared, blocking the way and searching him. Just as the situation was critical, a large number of villagers were returning home from the town. Zhang shouted loudly for help. The bandits saw the large number of people and fled.

Demolishing the Moon City: The four Moon Cities in this county, except for the South Moon City, which was demolished last year, the East, West, and North Moon Cities have been repeatedly requested to be demolished, but have not yet been implemented. It has now been approved, and the North Moon City began demolition on the 25th. It is reported that the East and West Moon Cities will also be demolished.

Songjiang

Inspection of Boy Scout by Training Supervisor's Office: The Training Supervisor's Office of the National Government dispatched Inspector Chen to Songjiang yesterday to inspect the student army at Songjiang Provincial Middle School. At 1:00 PM, all the school's student soldiers assembled for inspection by Chen. After the inspection, a written examination was conducted, which Chen praised highly.

County Propaganda Department Convenes Student Discussions: To expand propaganda efforts, the Propaganda Department of the Songjiang County Consolidation Committee convened a meeting of student representatives from various schools on the afternoon of the 23rd. Chairman Wang Tianren reported the significance of holding the discussion and discussed points of attention for future propaganda. It was proposed to organize a propaganda team, staffed by students from various schools every Sunday, to go out and spread propaganda. This was unanimously approved, and organizational plans are currently being drafted by the County Propaganda Department.

The 2nd Artillery Regiment Strictly Enforces Military Discipline: The commander of the 2nd Artillery Regiment of the Central Military Academy, Li Pinghuai, led his troops to Songjiang and stationed them in the old Tishe gunpowder depot barracks. They are engaged in daily training, and military discipline is strict. Yesterday, Commander Li issued a six-character rhyme proclamation to the citizens, declaring the regiment's discipline, promising to protect the local area, and urging the public to live and work in peace.

Financial Bureau Rectifies Tax Deeds: She Yingduo, the director of the County Finance Bureau, previously visited Songjiang with an inspector from the Finance Department. Regarding the concealment of tax deeds and underreporting of property values, they jointly proposed three rectification measures, which were submitted to the Finance Department and approved. Now, Director She has formulated various reporting forms and sent them to the district offices for distribution to townships and police stations for compliance. The rectification measures are as follows: (1) When people pawn or sell real estate, the land guard must be present to certify the deed. Therefore, the land guard is most aware of field and house transactions. Now, the bureau has formulated a reporting form and distributed it to the land guards, instructing them to fill in the transaction information of real estate within the map at any time and report it to the bureau at the end of the month for tax collection. If there is any concealment or collusion in underreporting the property value, a fine equal to that of the property owner will be imposed, and serious offenders will be investigated. (2) An order is issued to all compilers that they must rely on the push-and-collect certificate for transfer. A reporting form is formulated and distributed to each compiler, who must fill in each item during the transfer and compare it with the previous register when submitting the busy canal actual collection register. If there is any change in between that has not been included, it is considered concealment by the compiler, who shall be fined the same amount as the property owner. At the same time, an order is given to investigate the area under their jurisdiction at any time. If there is any private deed filling or underreporting of property value, they may report it to the bureau for punishment, and half of the fine will be awarded as a reward. (3) Substitute tax deed collection offices are set up in the four branch offices of Tinglin, Fengjing, Tianmashan, and Qibao. The deed tax silver will be turned over to the bureau once every five days. After the bureau fills in the deed, it will be returned to the respective branch offices for redistribution to the property owners for collection. At the same time, one-third of the handling fee charged by the branch office will be provided as a subsidy to the branch office.

Department Commissioner Inspects the Songwei County Road: Since the start of construction last winter, the roadbed of the Songwei County Road in this county has been gradually completed. The Construction Department has appointed Wu Wenhua, director of the Shanghai County Construction Bureau, as the inspection commissioner, who will arrive in Songjiang today (the 24th) and go to inspect it tomorrow.

Pudong Bandits Flee to Yangshan: The remnants of the Pudong gang led by bandit Tai Bao A Shu fled through the Liwan area southwest of Shanyang Town in Punan the day before yesterday. Leading more than 60 bandits in 12 boats, each carrying long guns, box cannons, and sharp blades, they were intercepted by the first team of the Songjiang Water Police. The bandits were defeated and retreated, and the fourth brigade of the Anti-Smuggling Unit intercepted two empty boats and six people, including Nei Piao Xu Asheng. Now, after the remnants broke through the encirclement, they passed through Baziqiao and hijacked two large sampans owned by Jiang Jiesheng, driving them out to sea and fleeing into Yangshan. Jiang Jiesheng escaped alone. More than ten small boats left behind by the bandits, including two better Luxu boats, were moored in the Shanyang City River and guarded by the Public Security Bureau. There are also several bandit boats temporarily left to await reporting to the authorities. He Yalin, the captain of the First Water Police Team, fought with the bandits this time and seized firearms, some of which were stolen from Zhejiang. He has prepared a document and reported it to the district headquarters.

Hunan Refugees Pass Through the Border Harassing the City: Three hundred refugees from Xiangxiang, Hunan, arrived in Taibo City, Fangqiao Town, this county, the day before yesterday. They came by eight boats from Wuxian. After arriving, they set fire to the road. Then, they went to Dangkou and Hongshengli to land and harass in Nanxiang. The villagers were unable to resist. A certain surname's family was robbed of two gold rings, a pair of gold bracelets, and a package of clothes, worth about a hundred yuan. Then, they went to Guanlian Bridge and wanted to land again. The villagers sounded the alarm, and then they left. Then, at Miaoxiang Bridge, they robbed a woman watching the temple of four silver yuan. The local security guard of the town gathered more than twenty yuan in foreign currency to give them, and the patrol officer of the Hongshengli Public Security Bureau sent police to escort them out of the border.

Nantong

The Finance Department Sends Personnel to Inspect Northern Jiangsu Finance: Xie Qinsheng, a commissioner sent by the Finance Department, came to Tong to inspect the tax collection situation of the Finance Bureau. On the 25th, he went to Rugao, Taiyang, Jingdong, and Xinghua counties for inspection.

Please Exempt Troops and Police from Being Transferred to Suppress Bandits: The national army and provincial police team who are suppressing bandits in Tongyi are now ordered to leave Tong. Local communities in Tongyi are afraid that the banditry is not yet suppressed, and they have telegraphed the headquarters and the provincial government, appealing for a temporary exemption from transfer to ensure the safety of the local area.

Anti-Banditry Conference in Tong and Rugao Counties: Representatives of the party, government, military, and police agencies of Nantong and Rugao counties will hold a joint anti-banditry conference in Tongcheng on the 30th of this month to discuss and determine methods. Tongyi held a preparatory meeting on the 25th to discuss anti-banditry preparations.

County Magistrate Zhang Appoints Officials: The newly appointed County Magistrate Zhang Dong took office on the 24th and announced the appointment of officials in various departments: Zhang Zunshi as Secretary, Zhao Jianhua as Director of the First Department, Wang Shanyu as Director of the Second Department, Sun Zongying as Accounting Director, Jiang Qisun as Receiving and Dispatching Director, and Zhang Aisun as General Affairs Director.

Jiangyin

The Zhanggujing Kidnapping Case Leads to the Arrest of Suspects: The Jinping, Jintong Bridge Security Corps in Shuangpai was informed that the family of Gu Zipei in Zhanggujing had been extorted by bandits and scheduled to go to collect the money. The corps received the news and waited in the wheat field. The night before, they saw five bandits, went forward to surround them, but unexpectedly, more than fifty bandits rushed out of the nearby Yaowang Temple. The two sides exchanged fire, and the bandits retreated. The Security Corps entered the temple and searched, and saw a suspicious monk, Shunfa, and a nun, who were both sent to the Public Security Bureau for handling.

Investigate the Total Amount of Grain Storage Revenue and Expenditure: The Ministry of Civil Affairs considers grain storage funds to be an important policy for disaster preparedness. The Jiangyin grain funds have been almost completely misappropriated. Liao Yaoxian was specially appointed to investigate in Cheng on the 24th to investigate the total amount of revenue and expenditure in detail for verification.

County Magistrate Shen's Lawsuit Case Searches for Evidence: The Ministry of Civil Affairs, based on Jiang Chuansheng and others' telegram alleging that Jiangyin's officialdom was corrupt, County Magistrate Shen and Director Zhang of the Public Security Bureau shielded opium, gambling, prostitutes, and red pills, and tolerated the chairman and members of a certain association, selling rice for export, known as the Five Poisons of Jiangyin. The Ministry of Civil Affairs sent Inspector Chen Jianming to investigate secretly and thoroughly, obtained conclusive evidence, and immediately dismissed County Magistrate Shen. Li Leng, the Director of the Public Security Bureau of Wujin, was appointed to act as the county seal. The Fourth Brigade Captain of the Provincial Police Force, Yu Shimei, was sent to lead two platoons to Wujin, and the newly appointed County Magistrate Li took a small wheel Xin Lianan and towed 15 civilian ships to Zhouzhuang from Chang on the morning of the 24th for concentration. At 2 pm, they walked to Zhangqing Gate, Shangsigang, and other places, first disarming the Security Corps on the gate, and searching Huang Bingzhong's home in the Reconnaissance Team, finding half a box of red pills, and the Caijiayuan red pill manufacturing mechanism, finding three boxes and a small piece of machinery. Huang Bingzhong's son, Zhao Zifang, Jiang Weizeng, and other four were arrested. Li interrogated them in the township administration bureau. Because it was late that day, they could not go to the city, so they temporarily stationed at Zhanwen Bridge and waited until today (the 25th) to take office in the city and handle everything.

Zhenjiang

The Ministry of Civil Affairs and Construction Implements Austerity Policies: The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Civil Affairs used to have six sections internally, with two additional secretarial and police departments. The total annual expenditure was about 345,000 yuan, or 34,000 yuan per month. The new budget is about 445,000 yuan per year, or 37,000 yuan per month. Now, due to the exhaustion of the provincial treasury, Minister Hu has implemented austerity policies, and very few personnel have been announced for various sections. It is planned to carefully identify and determine who will leave and stay. In addition, with the establishment of the Provincial Security Office, it is planned to transfer the original Third Section in charge of public security and the Fourth Section in charge of water police to the office to save expenses. In addition, the Construction Department originally had five sections in charge of construction, water conservancy, industry and commerce, finance, accounting, and general affairs. Now, Minister Sun believes that the department's expenses have been resolved by the provincial government meeting, reducing 1,000 yuan per month, so the internal contraction should be carried out to balance revenue and expenditure. Therefore, it is planned to merge the original five sections into four sections, that is, the Third Section in charge of industry and commerce will be merged into the Second Section, which will be implemented soon.

The Chamber of Commerce Asks to Exempt Tax on the Transportation of Foreign Rice: The Zhenjiang Chamber of Commerce stated that the province of Jiangsu suffered a famine last year, especially in northern Jiangsu. At this time when the green and yellow are not connected, there is no source, and rice prices are gradually rising. The counties have to raise funds and purchase foreign rice from outside ports to help the people. However, there are still several months before the autumn harvest, and it is necessary to purchase and handle them continuously to be able to provide continuous assistance. The price of rice is high, and the people's livelihood is difficult. It is not enough to maintain the people's food without facilitating transportation and reducing the burden. In view of the difficulties of the people, and in order to appeal on their behalf, the Ministry of Finance was telegraphed yesterday, hoping that the disaster-stricken areas of Jiangsu Province would be considered wide, and the people's food would be difficult. When this foreign rice passes through various customs stations, it will be temporarily exempted from tax for three months, and all customs stations will be notified to comply with it to benefit the disaster victims.

Yangzhou

Supervisor Arrests Kidnapping Bandits and Hostages: Li Zheng, the Supervisor of the Public Security Bureau, led the police to Niuzhuang, Ganquan Mountain the day before yesterday and arrested the female Xiao Ganzi, who was kidnapped, and two bandits, Zhou Fusheng and Bao Lianke. Yesterday (the 23rd), they were escorted to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

The Case of False Accusation of the Director Has Been Clarified: The Transportation Department ordered Zeng Chong, the former company commander of the Huainan Anti-Smuggling Camp, to accuse Tang Ken, the Director of the Anti-Smuggling Bureau. The department secretly investigated and dispatched Hu Xianrui, the second section chief of the department, to investigate and reply to each allegation. It has now been clarified that Lü Rong was suspected of colluding with bandits and left his post on his own. Later, he sought a career with Tang but failed. This time's accusation is purely fabricated. Yesterday (the 23rd), Hu truthfully presented the case to the department through the company.

He immediately went to the County Party Headquarters for inspection and then went to the district party headquarters and district branches for inspection. It is reported that Yang will go to Pinghu for inspection after completing the inspection in He.

Telegraph to Request Protection of the Cocoon Factory: The sericulture affairs in Jiaxing's four townships are about to be completed in a blink of an eye. Each cocoon factory is raising funds and taking posts in order to collect cocoons at the time. However, due to the influx of local bandits in recent times, robberies are frequent, and cocoon merchants dare not raise funds to collect cocoons, resulting in the contracts signed with the factory owners being cancelled one after another. The original cocoon trade has not even been renewed by two-tenths. Now, the Six County Cocoon Industry Association of Jiasu telegraphed the province yesterday, requesting maintenance measures.

Selling the Old Xie Office Building is Not Allowed: The old Xie Office in Jiaxing City is currently occupied by the Second District Department of the Water Police. Recently, District Chief Zhao Tingyu moved the district department to the Lanxi Guild Hall in Dongmen and sold the old Xie Office building to raise funds for the relocation. The district department sent a letter to the county to report to the province for approval. It is now learned that after the Civil Finance and Construction Department received the report, the old Xie Office was originally borrowed by the Water Police District Department and was not allocated for use. This building must be reserved for future public use. The requested sale is difficult to approve.

Jiashan

Alarm of Lake Bandits in Dongwang Village: At noon on the 24th, a large gang of lake bandits (rumored to be a merger of Taibao Ashu, who was defeated and retreated, and a small gang), 97 boats, were moored in the Dongwang Village area of ​​Zhao Xiong, three miles away from Dingzha, on the border of Jiangsu and Zhejiang. Rumors spread that they were planning to rob a certain large town nearby. After receiving the report, the local authorities immediately telegraphed District Chief Zhao of Jiaxing, who personally led the Yiwu and Gonghe warships and twenty teacher ships to encircle and suppress them from the south. The seventh team was ordered to take the north road, and Taozhuang, Luxu, and Jinze were to be encircled and suppressed. The eighth team's patrol team took the middle road, and the Zhiguo warship Shangwu Ningxing two rounds towed more than 30 teacher ships from Xitang out of Xiangfu Dang to attack Dingzha head-on. At dusk, there were gunshots, which seemed to be contact between the two sides, but the details are unknown.

Refugees Harass the Area: More than two hundred refugees from Xiangtan are now in the southeastern countryside of Xitang in this county, forcibly robbing and extorting, even kidnapping people for ransom and forcing extortion. The villagers in more than twenty villages nearby dare not live at home and fled to the city to take temporary shelter. On the afternoon of the 24th, they advanced towards Xitang and rested in the Dongyue Temple, a few miles away from the town. It is said that many of the refugees have firearms. The townspeople are panicked, and the competent authorities dare not suppress them. It is rumored that this group of refugees is under the eyes of bandits, so they have such a momentum.

Pinghu

The Appeal Case Has Been Adjudicated: Zhao Xinwen (ie Zhao Jiakui) outside the East Gate of this city was arrested in January of this year for a tobacco case. The county government sentenced him to two months in prison and fined him 300 yuan. Zhao refused to accept the verdict and appealed to the Hangzhou Higher Court. It is now learned that the High Court revoked the original verdict regarding the sentencing part and changed the sentence to two months in prison and a fine of 100 yuan.

Provincial Government Sends Team to Zhuji to Suppress Bandits: According to a long-distance telephone report from County Magistrates Xu of Zhuji and Qi, more than 2,000 agricultural troops were in contact with bandits, looting Sandu Town, and the bandits in the southeast rose up in response. The Provincial Government specially dispatched Battalion Commander Chen Zhifan of the Sixth Regiment to lead a team to suppress and defend yesterday.

Although the reinforcements arrived quickly, the loss was not great, but the residents were already frightened birds, and they moved to other places, resulting in ninety percent of the houses being empty and desolate. Yesterday, someone from Changxing talked about the fact that the business market in Sian had no one cent of transaction all day long.

Yesterday, it ordered the Ministries of Finance and Construction to jointly review and report the seizure.

New and Old Police Chiefs of Hang City: Li Zizai, the police chief of Hang, was dismissed and investigated for the case. He has now been transferred to the court for questioning for three hours. The content is complicated, and many people are involved. It is necessary to continue to study and question. The points of unauthorized fines and encroachment on legal rights have been confirmed. Yan Youfu, the new police chief, took office yesterday after being commissioned and will take an oath on a scheduled date after asking the Ministry of Civil Affairs.

Zhuji

The Entire Town of Sandu Was Robbed: After the giant bandit Wu Guifa was wiped out in Zhuji, Zhejiang, the territory was relatively peaceful in recent years. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the 22nd of this month, a large number of bandits suddenly appeared in Sandu, the county, with an estimated total of more than 3,000 people. They moved in groups, raged to the town, first robbed the police station of firearms, and then looted all the stores, leaving the town empty. County Magistrate Xu of the county heard the alarm and immediately telegraphed the Department of Civil Affairs to dispatch troops to encircle and suppress them on the 23rd. It is reported that the Department of Civil Affairs has consulted the Security Department to quickly prevent and suppress them.

Xiaoshan

The Shaoshan Automobile Accident Caused Damage: At 8 am on the 24th, the Shaoshan Provincial Highway automobile overturned into the mud when it was heading from Jiangqian to Xiaoshan and passing the Xixing Station because the driver was careless. At that time, an old woman surnamed Mo in the urban area was crushed to death, and six passengers were seriously injured. The rescue vehicle immediately sent all the injured to Xiaocheng Jimin Hospital for treatment. It is not known whether the two seriously injured can avoid the sorrow of life.

The Money Industry Agreed on Long-Term Interest Rates: In addition to the current flow, the money industry in Shaoshan has a long-term item, with a term of six months. It is released at the end of every March and September. After the implementation of the national calendar, it was changed to the end of April. Now that the release period for this long-term item has arrived, all interest rates have been agreed. Fellow trades pay 9 yuan and 25 cents per thousand per month, totaling 55 yuan and 50 cents. Foreign trades pay 9 yuan and 50 cents per thousand per month, totaling 57 yuan.

The Difficulty of Collecting Autonomous Donations: The Xiaoshan County Government previously ordered each village association to collect autonomous donations and set the donation rate for cultivated land and business rent interest income into four grades of A, B, C, and D, and collect them from each household. However, the countryside has been hit by disasters for years, and in handling land declarations, all business households with a little property have been ransacked. Now that we are collecting autonomous donations again, most households are embarrassed. Also, the village chiefs are not well-behaved, and they specialize in extortion, which is especially undesirable by the local people. Therefore, it is quite difficult to handle this donation.

Shaoxing

Now that the cocoon collection period is approaching, the bureau has notified all agencies to comply with it.

Send Personnel to Investigate the Disaster Situation in Xixiang: Due to the severe disaster situation in Xixiang, Xialv Bridge, and other places, He Keyuan was sent by County Magistrate Tang yesterday to investigate and find ways to provide relief.

The Deadline for Borrowing Construction Public Bonds to Be Submitted: Shaoxing has recognized a loan of 400,000 yuan for construction public bonds. Except for the first phase of 100,000 yuan in March, which has already been submitted, the second phase in April is approaching. County Magistrate Tang has set a deadline for the 27th to pay the full amount.

Important News

Hubei and Jinan

Resolution of Scout Conflict

The Hubei team has returned to Hubei. The Jinan University President gave a lecture and dealt with the scouts involved.

Details of the Conflict

Although this National Boy Scout General Inspection encountered various inconveniences due to weather and location, the organizing office made every effort to ensure the participating Boy Scouts endured hardship and persevered. From the inspection on the 18th to the opening and closing ceremonies on the 22nd, everything proceeded smoothly. The objectives of the general inspection, grand encampment, and performances were fully achieved and were quite impressive. After the closing ceremony, at 6 PM on the 22nd, as the scout troops were preparing to return to their respective places, unfortunately, a misunderstanding arose between the Jinan Scouts and the Hubei Scouts, initially due to language barriers, leading to verbal disputes and a conflict. This caused aftershocks from the closing ceremony. Various newspapers in Nanjing have already reported on this matter, but the accounts were inaccurate and contained errors. An important official from the organizing office discussed the actual events, which are recorded as follows: The Jinan Scouts had attempted to steal from the camp. On the evening of the 22nd, the Hubei Scouts were packing, preparing to leave the camp that night by boat to the west. They sent someone to the Jinan Scout troop to retrieve leather shoes and other items. The person sent had a Hubei accent. Most of the Jinan Scouts were children of overseas Chinese. Due to the language barrier, a misunderstanding arose, leading to a dispute. Initially, it was only a verbal argument, but then more and more scouts from both sides gathered, deepening the misunderstanding, which led to physical fighting. At that time, an important official from the organizing office was away on other important business, and the officials present tried to dissuade them, but due to the large and noisy crowd, they were unable to resolve the misunderstanding. Several of the younger Hubei Scouts fell in the mud or were hit by fists, feet, or sticks and were injured. During the chaos, someone from the Jinan side brought a shotgun used for camping and fired two shots into the air to intimidate, further disrupting order. Fortunately, the important official from the organizing office heard the news and rushed back, immediately stopping the situation and ordering all the scouts to return to their tents to restore order. By then, it was already dark, and all the boys and girls were terrified by the disturbance. The organizing office then requested the officers of the army unit stationed there to be on alert and sent personnel to explain the situation to each troop, so everyone could sleep peacefully. The injured were immediately given appropriate medical treatment by the hygiene department, and the Jinan Scout troop leader, a Mr. Chen, and a student团 who unauthorized fired the shotgun were detained to be disciplined by the Scout Headquarters according to Scout regulations. The remaining Jinan Scouts returned to Shanghai that night. The Hubei Scouts, due to the injured requiring medical treatment, delayed their departure from Nanjing. It is reported that the injured have been examined by the hygiene department, and none have life-threatening injuries. They have been sent to the Central Treatment Room and the Central Hospital for quiet recuperation. Therefore, the majority of the Hubei Scouts departed for Xiaguan today (the 24th) to await a boat back to Hubei. It is also reported that after the incident that night, Jinan University President Zheng Hongnian rushed to the organizing office upon hearing the news and severely reprimanded the leader of the school's scout troop. He also went to the Hubei Scout camp to express his sympathy to the Hubei Scouts. Everyone was very calm, and all misunderstandings had been cleared up. It is also reported that the Scout Headquarters has decided on appropriate punishments for the troop leader who caused the trouble and the member who fired the gun. The members of the troops involved in the incident were all young students in the lower grades of Jinan University.

I went to congratulate him and asked Mr. Cai to write a letter to Mr. Jiang Menglin to take care of our students. Two friends who were present frowned and said, 'Your school students often hit people. It's a bit scary.' I said that wouldn't happen. I guaranteed it. Another time, students from Central University behaved disrespectfully towards our students. Our students were able to endure it. They ran to my house that night. I was very pleased with their forbearance. However, I was a little dissatisfied because some things were published in the newspapers afterward. I don't think this kind of behavior is right. In the past three years, our school students have not only had a good position in sports but also made great progress in self-cultivation. I am always very pleased with this. A Review of the Second National Education Conference (2)

II. Preliminary Plan for Implementing Compulsory Education

(I) General Principles

(A) Objectives

(1) To ensure that all 40 million school-age children across the country who are not in school receive four years of compulsory education.

(2) For children who cannot continue in school for four years, to flexibly adjust the schooling period through supplementary education or self-study systems to make up for the compulsory education they should receive.

(B) Timeframe

(1) Within five years, complete the establishment of national teacher training institutions and simultaneously open 1,500 pilot areas for compulsory education in cities and rural areas.

(2) Gradually expand thereafter, and within 20 years, implement four years of compulsory education nationwide.

(II) Cultivating Teachers and Methods for Phased Enrollment of Children

(1) Approximately 200,000 teachers are needed for urban primary schools. Existing secondary teacher training institutions in cities are responsible for training them. Approximately 1.2 million teachers are needed for rural primary schools. Each county nationwide should establish 1,500 rural normal schools within five years, responsible for training them, with an average of 800 graduates per school. From the sixth year onwards, each school should have an average of 53 graduates per year.

(2) Teachers for urban normal schools are to be trained by existing normal universities or education colleges of various universities.

(3) A total of 21,000 teachers are needed for county-level rural normal schools nationwide. The provinces are to establish 27 rural normal colleges and normal departments of normal colleges, responsible for training them. From the second year to the fourth year, each province and each institution must train 180 teachers.

(4) 540 teachers are needed for provincial rural normal colleges and specialized departments. The National Compulsory Education College is responsible for training them in two years, cultivating 270 people each year. Thereafter, continue to train 200 people each year to fill vacancies.

(5) The National Compulsory Education College and pilot areas should establish two pilot areas in the first year, one in a city and one in a rural area, for student experimentation and to serve as a foundation for promoting compulsory education nationwide.

(6) Provincial normal colleges, specialized departments, and provincial compulsory education pilot areas should also be established in the second year, with urban and rural pilot areas also.

(7) County normal schools should be established in three phases, one-third in the third year, the fourth year, and the fifth year, respectively. From the third year to the fifth year, 500 county normal schools should be added each year nationwide, along with 500 urban and rural pilot areas.

(8) From the sixth year onwards, a net increase of 75,500 teachers per year can increase 75,000 primary schools, educating 3 million children. By the 18th year, primary schools will be universally established nationwide, and compulsory education will be fully implemented in the 20th year.

(9) In addition to teacher training, the following matters should also be handled:

(A) Register all normal school graduates in the province.

(B) Strictly enforce the service regulations for normal school graduates, requiring them to serve for two to five years.

(C) Assess primary school teachers who are not formal normal school graduates.

(D) Train unqualified teachers for one or two years.

(E) Examine teachers in private schools. Those who pass are allowed to be primary school teachers; those who fail are required to attend county normal school for two years of supplementary study.

(III) Methods for Increasing Classrooms

(1) Utilize ancestral temples nationwide.

(2) Utilize academies and public venues.

(3) Utilize all temples and monasteries.

(4) Reward private individuals for donating houses or funds to build school buildings.

(5) Publicly construct school buildings that are economical and durable.

Our school's scouts only had 40 people, so we had to fight back bravely. However, we are deeply ashamed and remorseful for this incident and are willing to accept the strictest punishment." Local News

The Library Undertakings of Liaoning Province

A Conversation with Mr. Bian Zongmeng, Director of the Provincial Library

Recently, the Liaoning Education Delegation went south to visit the educational achievements of Jiangsu and Zhejiang. In addition to the principals of various primary and secondary schools, Mr. Bian Zongmeng, the director of the Liaoning Provincial Library, also accompanied the delegation. The reporter spoke to him yesterday and inquired about the library undertakings in the Northeast. Mr. Bian's remarks were quite detailed and are summarized below:

In recent years, education in Liaoning has made considerable progress, and no effort has been spared to expand and develop social education. Taking libraries as an example, although there is only one provincial library (as Bian referred to his own), efforts have been made to increase funding in the 18th annual budget last year to strengthen it. I also arrived at the library at that time and greatly improved the library's operations, such as reorganizing old collections, increasing the purchase of new books, and adding children's reading rooms and popular lectures. Over the past few months, the results have been visible. The current collection includes more than 35,000 types of books, totaling over 102,000 volumes. Chinese books account for about two-thirds of the collection, with both old and new Chinese books in equal measure. Important old books, such as the Complete Collection of Illustrations and Books, are mostly available. The average daily number of readers reaches over 80, mostly students. In addition to our library, most counties have county libraries, currently totaling over 40. Although many are being reorganized, they are all expected to develop in the future. The provincial and county libraries are jointly organizing a library association, which is currently being planned and is expected to be realized this year. As for school libraries, all primary and secondary schools have libraries. However, the Northeast University has the most books. The university's new library building is under construction and is quite large in scale. The university's books were previously stored separately in various departments and were not managed systematically. In the future, when the new building is completed, there will definitely be a new reorganization. The old collection of the Siku Quanshu in the Wen Yuan Pavilion in the provincial capital has been completely copied and supplemented, but it is still stored and not open to the public. In the future, it may be organized and made public. In addition, what is most noteworthy is that the Japanese have established many libraries in the Northeast and pay great attention to collecting literature about the Northeast (adding a so-called "Manchuria-Mongolia" category in addition to the usual ten categories). Most of the libraries are located along the South Manchurian Railway, totaling 37. There are seven libraries in Dalian alone, and two in Shenyang. In addition, all major stations have them. Those without libraries have mobile libraries to ensure that all places with Japanese residents have libraries for their convenience. Looking back at our country, we are truly ashamed. Last year, I visited many of the libraries established by the Japanese and drafted a report to inform our countrymen, hoping that they would pay close attention to it. I have visited 16 libraries in Jiangsu and Zhejiang on this trip, each with its own strengths and merits. I will make many suggestions for the improvement of our provincial library after returning, which should not be in vain, he said.

Passing Items of Work for Staff

On Organizing the Scout Plan

The Party Education Section of the Training Department of the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department held its first section meeting yesterday, chaired by Zhu Jiarang, with Hu Yanyun as the recorder. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

Day One Record

Jinan University Sports Meet

Undiminished by Rain

And Able to Set New Records

Yesterday was the first day of the National Jinan University Spring Sports Meet. Although the weather was uncooperative, with wind and rain, the spirit was undiminished, and indeed felt even more courageous. It is truly because the athletes of this school possess outstanding talent, learning from each other to promote progress, and encouraging each other through competition. This time, the number of male and female students participating in sports exceeded one hundred, surpassing the number of previous sessions. The school suspended classes for two days. The law department, located in Shanghai, also returned to Zhenru yesterday to participate. Furthermore, local men and women, long admiring the reputation of Jinan University's sports meet, flocked to watch, with many carrying cameras to take photographs, an endless stream. The parking lot in front of the school was almost completely full. Details are recorded as follows:

Overview of the Venue

The venue is in the school's newly opened sports area. Although the Tai Chi room and gymnasium within the area have not yet been completed, the grounds have been leveled and arranged in an orderly manner. Located in the eastern part of the school, Zhiyuan Hall stands majestically in the northwest. The southeast borders the suburbs, with lush trees and beautiful scenery. The surroundings of the field are covered in green grass, adding to the natural beauty. The command platform is located in the north of the center of the field, using the soccer goalposts, with party and national flags hanging from the corners, fluttering in the wind, their colors appearing even fresher and more vibrant due to the rain. A portrait of the late Premier Sun Yat-sen hangs in the middle, with a stage about half a丈 high set below. To the west of the field, the trees are used as a barrier, with bamboo separating the spectators' standing area. Further west, in an open space, three or four Boy Scout tents are set up for the athletes to rest.

Competition Results

Yesterday, due to the rain, the field was slippery because it was a newly developed area and the soil had not yet solidified. However, new records were still set in the Group A 100-meter race and high jump. If the weather had been clear, the results would have been even more amazing.

Local News

Umeya Shokichi Continues to Make

Sun Yat-sen Statue to be Shipped to China

Arriving in Shanghai on May 2nd

A letter from Japanese citizen Umeya Shokichi to this newspaper states: "To the esteemed editor, I am writing to inform you that I previously donated two bronze statues of Mr. Sun Yat-sen, which were erected in the capitals of China and Japan. I am deeply grateful for the warm welcome they received. To further my aspirations, I have commissioned the creation of five additional bronze statues of Mr. Sun Yat-sen in my country. These statues will be erected in important cities throughout your nation, including Beijing, Wuchang, Guangdong, and Zhongshan County, as a testament to my admiration. The statue intended for Guangdong (Whampoa Military Academy) has already been completed and will be transported to Shanghai on the Japanese ship Taiyo Maru at the end of April (arriving on May 2nd). From there, the military academy will dispatch a warship to escort it to Guangzhou. In addition to sending letters to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek of the National Government and the Guangdong authorities, I have also consulted with Mayor Zhang Qun. I will dispatch representatives to Shanghai to welcome the statue upon its arrival. This special letter is sent to inform you and request that you publish it in your newspaper for public awareness. Sincerely, Umeya Shokichi, April 24th, Republic of China Year 19."

Special Alert in the Concession

Due to the recent occurrence of major cases in the concession area, the Shanghai Municipal Council (SMC) of the International Settlement, in order to maintain public safety, in addition to constantly supervising Chinese and Western detectives patrolling the streets in plain clothes, announced a special alert starting at 5:00 AM this morning. An official order was also issued, notifying all twelve police stations in the International Settlement that all Chinese police officers are to remain stationed at their police stations, awaiting dispatch at any time, in order to mobilize when necessary.

Public Tram Strike in the International Settlement Yesterday

Tram Workers Present Nine Demands

Less than a week after the Shanghai Municipal Council (SMC) bus strike, drivers and ticket sellers of the British and American tram company also went on strike yesterday afternoon, causing all trams and trolleybuses running on various roads to come to a complete halt. According to the company, they did not receive any warning from the workers before the strike. However, according to worker sources, the demands had been submitted to the company two days prior but received no response, hence the strike was implemented yesterday. It is said that the reason for the strike is that after the tram fares were increased starting last Sunday, the daily revenue increased dramatically, reaching 1,400 yuan. The tram workers, feeling the pressure of rising prices and the cost of living, initiated a wage increase movement. Another reason is said to be that after the bus company workers went on strike, the company failed to accommodate the workers' demands and instead hired Russians to drive and sell tickets. The tram workers, feeling that this concerned the same public utility, went on strike in support. These rumors are compiled and recorded as follows:

Strike Process: Signs of a tram worker strike were already apparent the day before yesterday. On that day, the tram workers made a request to the company for an increase of seven cents per day for rice allowance. The company reportedly agreed at the time, and thus the day passed peacefully. Unexpectedly, at 6:00 AM yesterday morning, the time when the trams usually start running, about 700 drivers and ticket sellers at the old depot in Tilanqiao failed to report for duty. It was then that it became known that some tram workers had begun a strike. As a result, eastern district trams, such as Routes 6, 7, 8, and 9 trams, and Routes 17 and 18 trolleybuses, were immediately suspended starting early yesterday morning. By yesterday afternoon, the strike had spread to the new depot in Hart Road in the western district. Tram workers on Routes 1 and 2 drove their trams back to the depot and began striking. By 2:00 PM yesterday afternoon, the entire Shanghai Municipal Council (SMC) tram service had completely shut down.

Scope of the Strike: Trams and buses in the French Concession, except for those running on Shanghai Municipal Council (SMC) routes, were slightly affected. Otherwise, they continued to run as usual. Route 5 trams, operated by the French company, which run between the North Railway Station and the Ximen area, and Routes 17 and 18 trolleybuses, which must pass through the Shanghai Municipal Council (SMC), shortened their routes to run only between the borders of the French and International Settlements, not entering the Shanghai Municipal Council (SMC) area. Trams and buses in Nanshi and buses in Zhabei continued to run as usual.

Strike Conditions: The tram workers presented the following nine demands for the strike: (1) A uniform wage increase of eight yuan per month for each person. (2) A uniform rice allowance of three yuan per month for each person. (3) Recognition of the club's right to represent all workers, with the management subsidizing office expenses of 300 yuan per month. (4) Wages to be paid as usual during weekly holidays and festival holidays, with double pay for those who work. (5) Wages to be paid as usual for sick leave. (6) Wages to be paid as usual during the strike. (7) No workers to be dismissed and oppose the hiring of White Russians. (8) Release of arrested workers and no further arrests of workers. (9) Tea containers to be set up at all timekeeping stations.

Strike Discipline: (1) Absolutely obey the orders of the strike committee. (2) Actively participate in strike work. (3) Anyone who engages in the following disruptive behavior will be treated as a traitorous worker and rigorously dealt with: 1. Those who return to work privately without receiving a resumption of work order from the strike committee. 2. Those who engage in various propaganda to sabotage the strike. 3. Those who collude with capitalists and organs of worker oppression and inform the enemy. Shanghai International Settlement Tram Company Strike Committee, April 25th.

Company Attitude: According to the Ta Wan Pao, after the tram strike, reporters visited the company's general manager, Mr. Boggis. Mr. Boggis stated that the sudden strike was unexpected. When the company learned that trams in the Tilanqiao area had stopped running that morning, everyone in the company was surprised. Although there are various indications that could serve as reasons for the strike, the workers have not yet made any indication. The factory has not received any formal request for a salary increase. He believes that the matter is not for a salary increase. Mr. Boggis is currently waiting for the workers to formally notify him of the motives for the strike.

Taxpayers' Association Refutes

Macdonald's Fallacies

Chinese Support of Macdonald Registered Significantly, Creating His Position

Macdonald's Speech Presents Obsolete Ideas, Undermining Sino-Foreign Cooperation

Violating British Government's China Policy

Rendering British Government Declarations Worthless

The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers Association issued a Sino-English rebuttal yesterday to Mr. Macdonald's speech on the 16th of this month at the Ratepayers' Westerner Meeting. The Chinese version is recorded as follows:

The Shanghai Municipal Council's proposal to increase the number of Chinese directors by two this year was discussed at the Foreign Ratepayers' Meeting on April 16th of this year. Mr. Macdonald (a lawyer at the Godefroy law firm) gave a lengthy speech that incited the foreign ratepayers in attendance with his fanaticism, who blindly rejected the proposal. Chinese and foreigners alike deeply regretted this, recognizing that the spirit of Sino-foreign cooperation that had been built up over the years had been undermined. Mr. Macdonald should bear the responsibility for this, but the small number of foreign ratepayers in attendance who did not carefully consider the matter and hastily passed the rejection are also a major cause.

This association believes that Macdonald's speech, with its confused organization, obsolete ideas, fabricated facts, lack of evidence, and utter worthlessness, and the results it led to, are naturally invalid and do not warrant a rebuttal. However, out of love for the spirit of Sino-foreign cooperation that has been built up over the years, we cannot bear to see it destroyed in a single day, lest unfortunate events occur. We must say a word to the citizens of China and foreign nations. However, before rebutting Mr. Macdonald's speech, this association should transcribe its declaration below to clarify its position (This association affirms that foreign ratepayers in the Shanghai International Settlement have no right to discuss or decide on the civil rights that Chinese ratepayers in the International Settlement should have. Based on this principle, the rejection of the proposal to increase the number of Shanghai Municipal Council Chinese directors by two at the Foreign Ratepayers' Meeting on April 16th is naturally invalid. This is solemnly declared.)

Upon investigation, Mr. Macdonald's speech was emotional rather than rational, destructive rather than constructive, and resulted in difficulties for foreigners and resentment from Chinese. His ideas were obsolete and violated the spirit of the times. Mr. Macdonald even forgot that he was British, thus disregarding the British government's recent diplomatic policy towards China. The speech, in a long meeting, could not have had any effect except to be deemed unworthy of adoption and unable to be established. The foreign ratepayers' meeting in the International Settlement is similar in nature to a temporary gathering of citizens, and the vast majority of the ratepayers in attendance did not have a deep understanding of the matter. After his arrogant speech, ignoring Chinese sovereignty and disregarding the Chinese nation, they almost all forgot that they were in a meeting hall located on Chinese territory, with an absolute majority of Chinese citizens outside the meeting. They acted like a group of children being hypnotized, resulting in the inevitable blind obedience of mass psychology. This is truly due to the deficiencies of the meeting system. Otherwise, why would foreign public opinion have severely criticized the outcome of the case and advocated for remedies?

This association believes that Mr. Macdonald's actions have not only split all the citizens of the International Settlement into two opposing sides, but have also dealt a blow to the British government's recent efforts to restore the goodwill of the Chinese people. This is truly unfortunate for the people inside and outside the settlement, and also unfortunate for the British government.

This association has no responsibility to refute Mr. Macdonald's attacks on the Shanghai Municipal Council directors, his claims that the proposal was made under pressure, and the lack of sufficient reasons. As for whether Chinese directors support the declaration of the Shanghai Businessmen's Federation, this association believes that if the declaration of the Shanghai Businessmen's Federation is a fair proposition, then any Chinese person would support it. Otherwise, even if they wanted to support it, justice would not allow it. The May 30th Massacre was caused by the abuse of power by the Shanghai Municipal Council director at the time. In order to ensure the implementation of the spirit of cooperation, the Chinese directors mediated and resolved part of the compensation, thus helping the British people out of a predicament. The May 30th Martyrs' Cemetery and the families of the May 30th Martyrs voluntarily donated 20,000 yuan for compensation, and the remaining construction costs were donated by Chinese people. This commemorates the martyrs who sacrificed for justice and humanity on that day, and there are reasons for it in both reason and emotion. The Chinese people still think that the construction of the May 30th Martyrs' Cemetery is too small, and the compensation issue is still pending, which is regrettable. The existence or non-existence of an anti-foreign movement depends entirely on whether foreigners have unreasonably oppressed the Chinese people. However, the Chinese people are a rational nation. Seeing that the Chinese people have remained peaceful, calm, enduring, and bearing the burden of injustice after Mr. Macdonald's insulting speech, awaiting a judgment of fairness and justice, is sufficient proof that the talk of an anti-foreign movement is entirely Mr. Macdonald's fabrication. The Shanghai Municipal Council Chinese directors are naturally seeking the interests of the Chinese people, just as foreign directors are seeking the interests of the foreign people. Otherwise, the Shanghai Municipal Council directors should be elected by all citizens, regardless of nationality, in a mixed election, without the need to stipulate in fact how many seats for Chinese, how many for British, how many for American, and how many for Japanese. But do Chinese only seek the interests of Chinese people, and do foreigners not only seek the interests of foreign people? Please look at the Shanghai Municipal Council budget. Is more used for the benefit of foreigners, or is more used for the benefit of Chinese? For example, in educational expenses, do foreigners account for more, or do Chinese account for more? All of the Chinese people oppose the sale of the electricity department. The Shanghai Municipal Council Chinese directors are elected by the Chinese people, and naturally take the intentions of the Chinese people as their intentions. As far as this association knows, Mr. Macdonald is a lawyer at the British Godefroy law firm, and many Chinese people register with that law firm. Perhaps he obtained the qualification to attend the Foreign Ratepayers' Meeting because of the support of the Chinese people. Now, he benefits from the Chinese people but turns around and bites them, wantonly undermining the interests of the Chinese people, which is truly beyond reason and emotion. This association deeply sighs.

In his speech, Mr. Macdonald stated that it is not known whether the Chinese directors can represent the Chinese people, how they are elected, what their political views are, what their position is, and how many Chinese taxpayers there are. From these few words, this association feels extremely sorry for Mr. Macdonald. The election methods and number of taxpayers of this association and the election situation are all disclosed in the newspapers. Anyone who can read Chinese characters knows this. Perhaps Mr. Macdonald has this argument because he entered the country without knowing its writing. To criticize a social event, one must pay attention to daily facts. Mr. Macdonald knows nothing about the news of this association in the newspapers, and his remarks naturally mostly become fabricated facts. Even though he has lived in China for eighty or ninety years, he is still completely ignorant, let alone eight or nine years.

Mr. Macdonald also extensively cited the history of the government's colonial policy in India in his speech to incite the psychology of self-importance among the foreign ratepayers in attendance, further proving the obsolescence of his mind, setting aside the British government's recent diplomatic policy, and encouraging British ratepayers to betray the British government. At the same time, British people who are dedicated to professional pursuits and have no ambition for aggression while abroad risk seeing their professional standing shaken. This association feels particularly chilled on their behalf.

Mr. Macdonald quoted the imperial edict of the Qing Dynasty's Qianlong Emperor to the British Emperor in 1793 in his speech, further revealing his anti-Chinese ideology and attempting to use it to mobilize the foreign ratepayers in attendance to unite in an anti-Chinese movement. Whenever foreigners with aggressive ambitions encounter Chinese people seeking justice and resisting this kind of foreign oppression, they falsely accuse them of engaging in an anti-foreign movement. Like this kind of foreigner, both anti-Chinese and anti-foreign movements are not permitted by justice and fairness and should be corrected. Furthermore, the Qianlong era was a closed era, and its thinking was feudal and autocratic, which is not sufficient to represent the Chinese people of today. Moreover, this is just a kind of statement, which is less than the cruel behavior of the implementers of the three major massacres of May 30th, Wanhsien, and Shakee in the past five years.
