The Japanese Actively Assist in the Proposal to Increase Chinese Directors

Drafting Concrete Measures for Assistance

Meeting Set for Next Wednesday

Page 14

On the afternoon of the day before yesterday, the Japanese community in Shanghai convened a meeting of Japanese taxpayers to discuss the special taxpayers' meeting. All attendees unanimously supported the proposal to increase the number of Chinese directors. However, because only about thirty Japanese taxpayers were present that day, Directors Fukushima and Saito were concerned that the invitation was not comprehensive enough and that a consensus could not be reached. Therefore, after the meeting, they consulted with Mr. Hayashi Yūkichi, the president of the Japanese Residents Association, to determine concrete measures for active assistance. Mr. Fukushima and Mr. Saito were assigned to draft concrete measures for active assistance and distribute them to all Japanese taxpayers for careful study. A second meeting will be convened next Wednesday to finalize the measures. It is planned that all Japanese taxpayers will attend the special taxpayers' meeting on May 2nd and unanimously vote in favor of increasing the number of Chinese directors by two. This phenomenon is truly detrimental to the administration of the settlement. Liu Jiwen Sworn into Office Yesterday Morning

Yesterday Appointed Heads of Nine Sub-Customs Stations

The newly appointed Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, Liu Jiwen, arrived in Shanghai on the 21st of this month. He first went to the Superintendent's Office to take over affairs. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, the swearing-in ceremony was formally held in the main hall of the office. Zhang Qun, sent by the Central Party Headquarters and the Executive Yuan of the National Government, and Zhang Fuyun, Director of the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance, attended to oversee the oath. The grand occasion of yesterday is recorded below in detail:

Guests in Attendance: Those who went to the Customs Superintendent's Office yesterday morning to attend the ceremony, besides Mayor Zhang Qun and his wife and Customs Administration Director Zhang Fuyun, included Xiong Shihui, Commander of the Songhu Garrison; Tao Baichuan, representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters; Wu Zhennan, Director of the Coast Guard; Guo Chengen, Director of the Shanghai Arsenal; Guo Biao, Director of the Central Mint; Xu Weizhen, President of the Special District High Court Branch; Zhao Tieqiao, General Manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company; Chen Shiguang, Director of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs; Leng Jun, Magistrate of Shanghai County; Zhu Yan, Director of the Land Bureau; Sun Jianhou, representative of the Social Affairs Bureau; Zhao Zhihao, representative of the Public Safety Bureau; Zhou Chucai, Lin Kanghou, Zou Bingwen, Chen Bingqian, representatives of the National Anti-Opium Association, and over two hundred others.

Ceremony Proceedings: (1) Overseeing officials take their seats; (2) Guests take their seats; (3) Superintendent takes his seat; (4) Stand at attention; (5) Sing the Party song; (6) Bow three times to the Party flag, the national flag, and the portrait of the late Premier Sun Yat-sen; (7) Chairman (Zhang Qun) respectfully reads Premier Sun Yat-sen's last will; (8) Superintendent takes the oath; (9) Overseeing officials Zhang Qun and Zhang Fuyun deliver speeches; (10) Guests (Xiong Shihui and Tao Baichuan) deliver speeches; (11) Superintendent replies; (12) Photograph; (13) Refreshments; (14) Ceremony concludes.

Superintendent's Oath: I, [Name], solemnly swear to sincerely follow the late Premier Sun Yat-sen's will, implement the Three Principles of the People, uphold national laws, and strive to be loyal to my duty. I resolve never to employ useless personnel, never to engage in self-enrichment or corruption, and never to accept bribes. If I violate this oath, I am willing to accept the most severe punishment.

He followed the late Premier for more than ten years, directly receiving the Premier's teachings and showing excellent results in his work. In 1925, when the Northern Expedition began, I worked with Mr. Liu at the headquarters. At that time, Mr. Liu managed military provisions and made considerable contributions. After the establishment of the National Government, Mr. Liu was appointed mayor. Mr. Liu, during this initial period, did not fear difficulties, did not compromise, and did not avoid criticism in order to seek progress and success in his work. It can be said that he is the most loyal and diligent comrade of our party. Recently, due to accumulated overwork and heavy responsibilities, he intended to retire to study academics and investigate politics, but the National Government still entrusted him with the arduous task of Superintendent of the most important Jianghai Customs in the country. Mr. Liu has a long record of research on finance and is certain to be competent and contribute to national finance. Therefore, I dare to congratulate the nation on obtaining a talent. Recently, in Mr. Liu's office, I saw a slip of paper with the words "Integrity can be sold, but honor cannot be bought," which he kept on his desk to encourage himself and his colleagues. We can deeply believe that during Mr. Liu's tenure, he will be able to eliminate the accumulated bad habits of financial institutions and dispel people's doubts about financial institutions. I congratulate the nation, and I also congratulate Superintendent Liu personally.

Zhang Fuyun's Speech: (Abridged) In addition to managing regular customs revenue, the Customs handles matters between the Customs and the local people, which are reported by the Customs Superintendent or submitted to the government for decision. Xiong Shihui's Speech: (Abridged) Personal reflections: The Jianghai Customs is a Chinese customs. Why is it necessary for foreigners to manage tax revenue and set up a supervisory agency? When this system was first implemented, it was felt that British management of tax revenue was superior to that of our own people, resulting in the loss of major power and its inclusion in treaties. This is what we find most distressing. Shanghai is the world's largest commercial center, like Nantong compared to Dalian, the Pearl River basin compared to Guangzhou and Hong Kong, and Shanghai controls the Yangtze River basin. The Jianghai Customs is extremely important. Here, I have two hopes: (1) I hope the new Superintendent will fulfill his duties and reorganize the customs affairs; (2) Prepare to abolish foreign management of customs duties, so that Chinese management of tax revenue is truly superior to foreign management. During the Meiji Restoration in Japan, all navigation rights and postal services were entrusted to foreigners, with Japanese supervisors appointed. These supervisors constantly reorganized navigation rights and postal services until they were recovered. Looking at the roads in the former concessions of Hankou, Jiujiang, and Zhenjiang after their recovery, they are not as smooth as they used to be, indicating a lack of preparation. Superintendent Liu has had excellent results in the revolutionary process, so I deeply hope that after taking office, he will not only be able to rectify tax revenue but also further prepare to recover the self-management of tax revenue, in order to truly abolish unequal treaties.

Zhejiang Immigrants Depart Today

The First Batch Consists of Only Over Four Hundred People

The Zhejiang immigrants going to Liaoning to reclaim wasteland, departing from Shanghai, have been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. Because the disaster victims from Wenzhou can arrive in Shanghai last night, they are approved to be transported by the Huayang ship today. Yesterday, the reporter met the transportation commissioner, Mr. He Zhengrong, and was told about the transportation of immigrants and the wasteland reclamation, which is recorded below in detail:

Disaster Victims Arrived Last Night: The immigrants departing this time were initially set at 1,400, then changed to 800. Among them, Yueqing and Pingyang in Wenzhou suffered the most severe disasters last year, so the quota was also the largest. The rest, such as Taizhou, Zhuji, and Ruichang, each had only over thirty people. The first batch of more than three hundred people sent to Shanghai by the Shanghai-Hangzhou train had already boarded the Huayang ship yesterday. The remaining five hundred people from Wenzhou and Taizhou, who were supposed to come to Shanghai on the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Haiyan ship, were reported by the leading committee members Gao and Yao in a telegram that immigrants there could not be gathered as planned due to deep-rooted local sentiments. Currently, only about seventy people have reported and departed and are on the Haiyan ship, scheduled to arrive in Shanghai at 8:00 PM on the 25th. They will board the Huayang ship at the Jinliyuan Wharf that night. Therefore, only over four hundred people will be sent in the first batch. The disaster victims who boarded the ship last night were assigned cabins and managed by the committee members.

Departing Shanghai This Morning: The Zhejiang Provincial Government specially sent transportation chief Zheng Yu and commissioners He Zhengrong and Hu Ruyin to escort the immigrants along the way and accompany them on the ship. They are scheduled to leave Shanghai for Yingkou at 9:00 AM today. In the Northeast, Li Guangyu, Magistrate of Haiyan County, has been sent to Liaoning to take care of the immigrants' food and lodging after arriving in Shenyang and to liaise with the Liaoning Civil Affairs Department to distribute them to reclamation areas. A telegram has been sent to notify him. The expenses for this immigration are borne by the provincial government for those sent from Hangzhou and by the county governments for those sent from Wenzhou and Taizhou.

Wasteland Reclamation Plan: According to Commissioner He Zhengrong, the current population density in Zhejiang is about seventy people per square mile, almost the same as in Japan, while the eastern provinces have more land and fewer people, with only twelve or thirteen people per square mile. This time, the Zhejiang immigration to the Northeast is indeed the best way to seek a way out for the poor. It is not only beneficial to the people's livelihood and the national economy, but also the number of Japanese and Koreans reclaiming land in the Northeast has been increasing in recent years. A great source of profit is being occupied by foreigners, and it is also of great importance to our country's border defense. After the Zhejiang disaster victims arrive in Liaoning, they will be divided into two groups: the poor households with no assets will first be employed as laborers, while those with assets will claim land for self-cultivation, and the future development will be even greater.

Creating Irrigated Rice Fields in the Northeast: The Zhejiang investigation committee went to Liaoning last time and consulted with the Northeast authorities many times. Most of the currently cultivated land there is for sorghum, soybeans, and millet. It is planned to take advantage of this Zhejiang immigration to develop irrigated rice fields so that rice can be planted. The soil in the Northeast is four feet deep and suitable for planting, even more fertile than the soil in Jiangsu and Zhejiang. After opening up irrigated rice fields, fertilizer can be exempted for two years, with abundant harvests and low costs. The farmers will become richer faster than in the Southeast. Mr. He also said that after personally inspecting the situation in Liaoning this time, he is determined to go to various counties and villages in Zhejiang to vigorously promote and persuade farmers not to be bound by local sentiments and to go to the Northeast to exploit the treasures.

Eight Sick People Sent Back: Among the more than three hundred immigrants who came to Shanghai earlier, eight suddenly fell ill and could no longer go to Liaoning. The committee director Zheng Yu and others decided to stop their transfer, and they have already been sent back to their hometown yesterday.

Fifth Health Sports Meet

Scheduled to be Held on May 14th and 15th

The Health Sports Meet is held twice a year according to central regulations. It is an important policy of health administration to instill health knowledge in the public. If people can understand the importance of health, they will surely support it wholeheartedly. Even if they do not support public health, they will use appropriate methods to protect their own health. The Municipal Health Sports Meet was first created in this city. The first time was on a larger scale and attracted the most attention. Later, to save expenses, only small-scale propaganda was done. This year's (fifth) Health Sports Meet is planned to be held jointly with the Municipal Party Headquarters and various bureaus of the Municipal Government on May 14th and 15th. Traditional Chinese Medicine

Standards for Establishing Hospitals and Clinics

Approved by the Central Government

The Sixth District Party Headquarters of this city received a public letter No. 158 from the Municipal Party Headquarters yesterday, which said: "To the point, the Secretariat of the Central Government replied to a letter from your association, submitted by the Sixth District Party Headquarters, that the Municipal Health Bureau intends to change the name of traditional Chinese medicine hospitals to clinics, which is obviously a contempt for traditional Chinese medicine. It is suggested that all Chinese and Western hospitals, whether public or private, should be called hospitals or clinics, and be prefixed with the words 'Chinese' or 'Western' to show the difference, etc., and forwarded for review. After approval, it was decided that it is not appropriate to call Western medicine 'hospitals' and traditional Chinese medicine 'clinics' uniformly. However, it is also inappropriate to call public ones 'hospitals' and private ones 'clinics,' as suggested in the letter. The name of 'hospital' or 'clinic' should be based on the scale and completeness of the facilities. It is handed over to the Ministry of Health for proper review. This letter is recorded for reference." Afterwards, a reply was received in letter No. 366 (meeting character 5935), which briefly stated, "Regarding the issue of hospital names, the Ministry has carefully reviewed it and believes that the letter's statement that the name of 'hospital' or 'clinic' should be based on the scale and completeness of the facilities is appropriate and should be promoted. Now, traditional Chinese medicine hospitals in various places that have considerable scale and equipment can also be allowed to have the name of traditional Chinese medicine hospital, and other measures should be formulated to manage them. Please check and forward this." etc. In accordance with the regulations, this is specially recorded and sent for reference. (Omission below)

Commodity Inspection Bureau Requests Strict Prohibition of Farmers Mixing Inferior Cocoons

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau believes that the silkworm season is approaching and silk cocoons will soon be on the market. Farmers are selling cocoons with good and bad ones mixed together, which damages the quality of the cocoons and affects the factories. Therefore, Director Zou submitted a request to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, requesting that the Ministry of Agriculture and Mines be consulted to order the provinces, cities, and counties to strictly prohibit this. The original request stated: "Regarding the matter of submitting a request, in recent years, silk factories in Jiangsu and Zhejiang have reduced silk production, and supply cannot meet demand. Every year at the end of the year, or before the new cocoons are on the market, they stop work to wait, which reduces the amount of silk produced. The waste of time and the stagnation of capital are deeply related to the future of the silk industry. In addition, the suspension of work by laborers and unemployment have a greater impact on people's livelihoods. The fundamental solution depends on improvement. The reason why the supply of raw silk is insufficient is due to the inability to expand the silkworm area and the poor breed of silkworms and poor feeding. However, farmers raise silkworms, and it does not matter whether the cocoons are good or bad when selling them. Therefore, they do not pay attention to the method of picking cocoons, and the number of double cocoons and rotten cocoons is increasing day by day, and the amount of silk cocoon material is gradually decreasing, which is also a major reason. On the other hand, in Japan, when silkworm farmers sell cocoons, all double cocoons, thin-skinned rotten cocoons are eliminated and not allowed to be mixed with high-quality raw cocoons. The price of the cocoons is also determined by the quality. Therefore, the cocoon farmers obtain high profits, and the factories also avoid intangible losses. In addition, with proper feeding and silkworm breeding, the production of good cocoons has increased sharply, and the number of inferior cocoons has naturally decreased. Later, it has surpassed us and taken away the first place in silk production in our country. If our country wants to save the situation, it must quickly catch up and quickly eliminate the various shortcomings mentioned above. The silkworm farmers mix inferior cocoons, which damages the factories. Shen Huachen, the former chairman of the Shanghai Silk Factory Association, once drafted a prohibition method and submitted it to the Ministry of Agriculture and Mines for approval and issued an order. However, the farmers have been ignoring it for a long time and continuing to mix inferior ones as before, which has become a habitual practice and is a major obstacle to the progress of the silk industry. In order to improve the quality of raw silk, the bureau should prepare a document stating the reasons and respectfully request your ministry to review it and consult the Ministry of Agriculture and Mines to reiterate the ban on mixing inferior cocoons when selling cocoons, and also consult the Nanjing and Shanghai special municipalities and the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui provincial governments to order the municipal and county governments to notify the silkworm farmers that when selling fresh cocoons, they must not mix double cocoons, thin-skinned rotten cocoons, etc., so that the quality is clearly distinguished. At the same time, order the cocoon industry associations and silk factory guilds in various cities and counties to specifically inform the cocoon businesses and silk factories to strictly set the grades when purchasing fresh cocoons, and increase the value of pure cocoons, and slightly increase the price of mixed cocoons, so that the general cocoon farmers will naturally tend to sell fresh cocoons and do not want to mix them. In addition, order the silkworm mulberry test fields in various counties to be responsible for sending personnel to promote and guide the farmers, inform them of the advantages and disadvantages, so that the quality of raw silk can be gradually improved, and foreign trade can also develop day by day."

More Local News Transferred to the Back Page

Page 15

Local News Two

Unprecedented Tragedy in Shanghai

Seven Lives Killed in One Family

The Night is Dark and All is Silent - Massacre Breaks out in Zhidel里

Master and Servant are Slain Together - The Life of a Six-Year-Old Child Should not have been Cut Short

Guo Chunsen Bedridden in Hospital, Narrowly Escaping Calamity

Axe and Knife as Murder Weapons ··· Servant and Maid Fled

Blood Congealed on Brocade Quilt ··· Corpses Strewn Throughout the Room

Siblings Rushed Back from School ··· Crying to Heaven at the Scene

Neighbors Filled with Dread ··· Police Paid Serious Attention

Yesterday morning around two o'clock, a massive case of family homicide involving seven people occurred suddenly at the residence of Guo Chunsen at No. 1169, Zhidelilong, Edwin Street, West Shanghai. Except for Guo himself, who was hospitalized due to illness at Baolong Hospital, and his two children who resided while studying at Fudan University, and his six-year-old eldest grandson, the entire household of seven, including male and female servants, were spared. The perpetrator(s) left behind two murder weapons, an axe and a kitchen knife, and fled without a trace. It was not until seven o'clock in the morning that the incident was discovered by neighbors, truly an unprecedented tragedy in Shanghai. The following is a detailed account based on the investigation conducted by our newspaper's reporter.

Once Served as Peace Negotiator Guo Chunsen, currently fifty years old, courtesy name Songnian, is from Guilin, Guangxi. He served as a member of the First National Assembly. In the seventh year of the Republic (1918), when the Northern and Southern governments were divided, the Northern government appointed Wang Yitang as the peace negotiator for the North-South negotiations. The Southern government had a seven-chief executive system of military government, with Cen Chunxuan as the chairman. Guo and Zeng Yan were both appointed as peace negotiators. Later, when Mo Rongxin served as the military governor of Guangdong, Guo served as the chief of staff of the governor's office. After Mo's departure in the ninth year of the Republic (1920), Guo left Guangdong and came to Shanghai, leisurely residing on the sea, living at No. 1169, the end of the first lane of Zhidelilong, Edwin Street, in the Public Concession.

A Glimpse of the Family Situation Guo's eldest son, Boqi, twenty-three years old, and his unmarried younger sister are studying at Fudan University as boarding students. Boqi married Liu Yanqiu, the daughter of Liu, a giant ship merchant from Xiamen, at the age of seventeen. The following year, she gave birth to a son named Susheng, who is currently six years old. In the following years, two more sons were born, one named Dasheng, four years old, and one named Meisheng, three years old. In addition, there is a male servant, a cook, three maids, and Guo's wife, née Li, currently forty-four years old, making a total of twelve people in the family. Except for the eldest son Boqi and his younger sister who reside at school, there are a total of ten people living at home.

Guo Chunsen Recuperating in Hospital Guo Chunsen served in politics in his early years. Recently, due to declining health, he suffered from various illnesses. Two months ago, he suffered from bubonic plague, and medical treatment was ineffective. Later, he sought treatment at Baolong Hospital, and he recovered and was discharged after about half a month. However, after the fourteenth of this month, he was hospitalized again at Baolong Hospital due to a leg ulcer, staying in room 107, costing about five yuan per day. Aside from one servant, no one else visited him regularly.

Tragic Cries in the Deep Night The area around Zhidelilong, Edwin Street, is located in the western district of the Public Concession. Few people walk around at night. Around two o'clock yesterday morning, the residents of Zhidelilong were all sound asleep. However, a tragedy was unfolding in Guo Chunsen's home at this time. The neighboring family of a certain surname suddenly heard continuous, tragic cries of "Ah yo!" from the Guo family. Although the sound was clear, they regarded it as someone else's business and unrelated to themselves. Moreover, according to Shanghai's customs, people are unwilling to interfere in external affairs, and neighbors in the lane do not even know each other's names. At that time, the Guo family's cries were thought to be the master scolding the servants, so they remained unconcerned, unaware that a great unprecedented tragedy was unfolding in the Guo family.

Child's Cries Reported the Massacre Guo's eldest grandson, Susheng, only six years old, went out the back door around seven o'clock yesterday morning. When a neighbor saw him, they recognized him as the young master of the Guo family. Wondering why he was out alone so early, they stopped him from leaving. Unexpectedly, Susheng immediately burst into tears, saying that everyone in his family was dead. The neighbor's face changed color upon hearing this, and more and more people gathered. At that moment, a bodyguard from the He residence, the landlord of Zhidelilong opposite, heard Guo's grandson's words and immediately went with several neighbors. The bodyguard took the lead and entered the house.

Blood Flowing Like a River in the Back Courtyard When the neighbors arrived at the Guo family's home, they saw blood flowing like a river in the back courtyard, with an unbearable stench. In the back room below, where the male servant Guo Song'an and the cook Guo Chaolong usually slept together, Guo Chaolong's head was seen to have been hacked open, with only a thin layer of skin connecting the head and neck. The blood was dripping, an extremely gruesome sight. The bedding and clothes were all stained red. A wood-splitting knife was left on the ground. The male servant Guo Song'an was nowhere to be seen. The neighbors immediately became suspicious, and one side sent someone to report to the police while the remaining people went upstairs to investigate, seeing a scene of horror.

Entire Family Wiped Out After receiving the news, the Jing'an Temple Road Police Station immediately ordered Chinese and foreign detectives to go to investigate. They found that Ms. Liu Yanqiu, Guo's daughter-in-law, was lying in the bedroom above the parlor, her head also having been chopped off. She was twenty-three years old. The third son, Meisheng, only three years old, was still in the same bed with his mother Liu, and was also killed. The attic was where the maids Conggui and Chunlian, as well as the eldest grandson Susheng and the second son Dasheng, lived. Except for Conggui, who had fled, the rest had their heads chopped off. The bedroom on the west side of the upper floor was Guo's wife Li's bedroom, and she was forty-four years old. She lived with the youngest maid, Qiulian. Both of their necks had also been chopped off. A kitchen knife was left beside the bed, stained with blood.

Returning Home Sick After Suffering a Great Calamity The Chinese and foreign detectives at the police station, seeing that the case was of great importance, immediately reported to the head of the police station, who personally went to investigate. For the sake of future investigation, the police station used electric light to take photographs and obtain the truth. At the same time, they notified Guo Chunsen, who was staying at Baolong Hospital. Upon hearing the news, Guo, with his family suffering a great calamity, had no choice but to return home sick. Seeing the tragic scene, he was overwhelmed with grief. Then he summoned his children back, only telling them that their mother had died of illness. The eldest son Boqi and his daughter, who were attending class at Fudan University, rushed over in a hired car upon hearing the alarming news. His nephew Guo Cang, who was studying at Jinan University, was also summoned home by Guo's family.

Siblings Crying to Heaven Upon arriving home, Guo Boqi and his sister saw that their loving mother, beloved wife, and beloved son had all been brutally murdered. They cried to heaven, overwhelmed with grief. Then they inspected the jewelry, clothing, and valuables, which had all disappeared. The estimated loss was over several thousand yuan. The male servant Guo Song'an and the maid Conggui took the valuable items and fled, which was beyond doubt. They were now under strong suspicion for the tragic deaths of the seven members of the family. According to their family members, this massacre was unexpected. The male servant Guo Song'an was twenty-three years old and was usually quite honest. However, two months ago, Guo and the maid Conggui often had a close relationship, which the mistress Li often scolded.

Liu Yanqiu's Brocade Quilt Covered in Blood When reporters arrived at Guo's residence, they saw a sea of people at the entrance of the alley, all trying to see the excitement. Police detectives guarded the door with guns. When reporters arrived at Guo's home, they saw the victim Guo Chunsen sitting in a corner, looking dazed. Later, his nephew Guo Cang received the reporters, who spoke with great sighs. The residence was two rooms and one wing. The interior furnishings were not very luxurious. After inspecting the upper floor, they felt nothing but sadness. The brocade quilts and embroidered rugs on the bed of Guo's young wife, Liu Yanqiu, were all stained with blood. Half of the light green printed silk quilt was dragging outside, and the blood that had flowed down had already congealed. The boxes and brocade boxes were messy. The top of the bed canopy was also splattered with blood, which was likely due to excessive force during the chopping. After inspecting the other rooms, the entire floor was covered with blood stains, a tragic sight. It was heard that his eldest grandson Susheng was able to escape this tragedy because the maid Conggui usually took care of him, and Susheng was still sound asleep when Conggui left.

Serious Attention from Various Police Stations The public concession police stations believed that such a serious case had occurred in West Shanghai, with bizarre circumstances and particularly cruel events. It was a rare tragedy in the concession. Therefore, Chinese and foreign detectives and inspectors from various police stations rushed to investigate. They also took the victim to nearby photo studios to view various photographic negatives in order to strictly arrest the perpetrators. The seven corpses of the Guo family were transported by car to the Ferren Road morgue yesterday morning. Due to the late hour, the examination was delayed. It was decided to request the Special District Court to come to the scene for examination this morning.

Bandit Robbery of a Car

Kidnapping of Bank Employee

Anhui Native Zhu Yian Kidnapped by Bandits

Bandits Rented a Car from Aidu Automobile Company

Drove the Chauffeur Off the Car Midway After Kidnapping Zhu

The Original Car Was Found on Jiangwan Road

Anhui merchant Zhu Lvsong, who started his business with yarn and also ran a pawnshop, lived at No. 250, Yongdingli, Shanhai Pass Road, Public Concession. His eldest son Yian, a young man, worked at the China Industrial Bank. He was kidnapped by bandits on his way to work at around 8:45 yesterday morning on Qingdao Road. There were a total of four bandits, three of whom had handguns. They had previously rented a car, No. 12538, from the Aidu Automobile Company on Aidu Road, instructing the chauffeur to drive to the scene of the incident. Waiting by the roadside, the bandits helped Zhu out of his private car, forced him into the rented car, and drove him away. Car No. 12538 was found on Jiangwan Road at around 3 p.m. The whereabouts of the hostage are unknown.

Luring the Prey Zhu Yian, twenty-one years old, works in the issuing department of the China Industrial Bank on Tianjin Road. His monthly income is very meager. He goes to work at nine o'clock every morning and hires a private car for transportation. Chauffeur Liu San has been working for many years, picking him up and dropping him off every morning. Zhu usually takes Xinza Road to go to work, but recently, due to road repairs, traffic was inconvenient, so he changed to Qingdao Road. Who knew he would fall into the hands of bandits because of this? Yesterday morning around 8:40, Zhu went out as usual. While traveling on Qingdao Road, two men suddenly flashed out halfway, approaching the chauffeur Liu San. They showed their colors, instructing him not to make a sound, and pressed a gun against Liu's back, coercing him to drag his young master into the alley. The chauffeur had no choice but to drag the car into the alley under the guidance of the gun. Seeing that there was no one around, the bandits dragged Zhu out of his seat and onto the car at the alley entrance and drove away. When Zhu was dragged out of his private car by the bandits, he was forced by the bandits' power and could not look back to see what his master was doing before he left, so he could not recount it in detail.

Burning Incense at Longhua The car left waiting at the alley entrance by the bandits was rented from the Aidu Automobile Company west of the Nanjing Grand Theater on Aidu Road. The time was around 7:40 in the morning. A middle-aged man in a long robe came to the Aidu Automobile Company, claiming that he wanted to rent a car to go to Longhua to burn incense. The customer spoke in a local accent, speaking calmly, and claiming to be a regular customer who hired cars. The accountant did not suspect anything else and immediately ordered chauffeur Xue A'gen from Changzhou to drive out a purple-red Buick sedan, No. 12538 (City 509), to respond to the customer. After the car drove out, it headed west. The person in the car told the chauffeur to drive to Changsha Road first, as there were incense guests waiting for them there, and then it would not be too late to go to Longhua. The chauffeur obeyed and immediately turned north and released Changsha Road. When they reached the middle of Qingdao Road, the customer ordered the car to stop, equal to the alley entrance.

Unbearable to Look Back The car stopped by the roadside for about twenty minutes. At first, no one came. The chauffeur probed the customer with words, and the customer said that waiting a little while would not hurt and said that there were also children going to Longhua for sightseeing. It must be because they were taking time to wash and dress. While speaking, he scratched his head and pretended to frown, as if he disliked waiting. The chauffeur believed it to be true and did not say much. Who knew that while he was sitting there bored, he suddenly felt two men suddenly come and jump onto the driving government? The chauffeur Xue A'gen couldn't help but be shocked. Just as he was about to open his mouth to ask, the gun had already appeared on both waists. Knowing that the situation was dire, he didn't dare to make a sound. After the two bandits got in, one took Xue's seat and replaced him, and the other sat on his left, and turned the mirror on the car window that could reflect the rear inward, so that the chauffeur would not have to worry about looking back. Suddenly, he heard the sound of the car door opening and closing, which seemed very urgent. Zhu Yian was hijacked into the car by the bandits at this time. The two bandits pointed their guns at the chauffeur's waist on both sides, and if he moved even slightly, a slap in the face would come. Therefore, although he heard the sound, it was unbearable to look back.

Scouts Everywhere After Zhu Yian was kidnapped and the car was robbed, the concession police authorities sent scouts everywhere to investigate his whereabouts. The Aidu Automobile Company also sent out cars to search for car No. 12538 in the countryside. In fact, after the bandits kidnapped Zhu into the car, they took the Beijing Road Bund to Broadway Road and drove to the vicinity of the Zhaofeng Road intersection. The bandits braked, opened the door, and ordered the chauffeur Xue A'gen to get out of the car, and then drove away, disappearing in an instant. Car No. 12538 was not reported to the Aidu Automobile Company by the chauffeur of the Hongkou Automobile Company until 3:00 p.m. that this car had been found on the cinder road near the Chizhi University on Jiangwan Road, and then the detective from the Xinzha Police Station was asked to come and drag the car back. According to the chauffeur of the Hongkou Automobile Company, he passed Jiangwan Road at about 10:00 a.m. and saw car No. 12538 parked on the roadside. At that time, he passed by in a hurry, thinking that the machinery was damaged and stopped there, so he did not feel cold. It was not until 3:00 p.m. that he passed through the area again, and the car was still in the same place, which he found very strange, so he notified the Aidu Automobile Company by phone.

Robbery of a Police Detective by Armed Robbers

Cao Xirong's Home Robbed

Guns Drawn, Exchanging Fire, Wounded

Suspicious Patient Arrived at Tongren Hospital

Suspected to Be Related to the Case

At 8:10 last night, Cao Xirong's home at No. 288, Qingyunli, Shaqin Road, East Jiaxing Road Bridge, Hongkou, who served as a police detective at the Tilanqiao Police Station, was suddenly robbed. The robbers opened fire to resist arrest, and both sides fought fiercely. The details are as follows:

Six Robbers Arrive Cao Xirong from Shandong, is currently serving as Police Detective No. 147 at the Tilanqiao Police Station in the Public Concession. His home is at No. 288, Qingyunli, Shaqin Road, East Jiaxing Road Bridge, Hongkou. At about 8:00 last night, six robbers suddenly came, using questioning as a reason to crowd in, drawing their guns to scare them into silence. First, they drove all the people in the house into one room, and then divided up to search. Two robbers kept watch downstairs, and four robbers went upstairs together.

Departure Home When the robbers were searching the house, Detective Cao was returning home from the police station. As soon as he entered the gate downstairs, the two robbers on watch knew that something was wrong and quickly looked up to warn the four robbers upstairs. The robbers then drew their guns and rushed downstairs, firing and fleeing. Detective Cao also drew his gun and returned fire. Both sides fired more than ten shots. The mixed number lasted about a few minutes. As a result, Detective Cao was shot in the head and twice in the right shoulder, immediately falling to the ground in pain. The robbers also took the opportunity to escape. Then, nearby detectives and arrests arrived after hearing the police and took Cao to the police station, and then transferred to the Shenjiawan Patrol Hospital. It was heard that the injuries were quite serious.

Pretending to Be the Victim About half an hour after the incident (8:45), a middle-aged woman suddenly accompanied a gunshot-wounded man to Tongren Hospital in Hongqiao for treatment. After the doctor examined him, he counted one bullet in the abdomen and one bullet in the left hip. He claimed to be Wen Zhuzheng, 37 years old, living next to the Laohuzao at the Datong Pier in the Sixteenth Barracks, a docker. Because he had thirty silver dollars with him, two robbers suddenly jumped out from the roadside when he passed the Jiaxing Road Bridge, showing their handguns. Because he resisted the robbers, he was shot, etc.

Reporting to the Police After the doctor asked in detail, he confirmed that it was a gunshot wound and immediately reported to the police station in charge by telephone. The head immediately ordered detectives to investigate. The language was unusually ambiguous and sent detectives to the supplied location to investigate the nearby detectives and the surrounding residents, who had not heard any police. And the estimated time and place of the incident coincided with the Cao Detective family robbery case. He immediately detained the woman and the injured person together and took them to the police station to investigate the truth and verify.

Problem of Dredging the Suzhou Creek

Construction Requires About Six Years

Chinese and Foreign Authorities Inspect

Regarding the dredging of the Wusong River (i.e., Suzhou Creek), since Director Song Ziliang of the Dredging Bureau has been keen to dredge, and because of construction issues, the Construction Committee has repeatedly met on dredging methods. It is heard that the Construction Committee has decided to organize a dredging committee for the Wusong River, together with the Shanghai Special Municipal Government to supervise the Dredging Bureau to carry out the work. However, this matter is of great importance. It is estimated that the dredging and revetment pier projects will be carried out in sections, requiring about six years. Director Song recently invited the Shanghai Special Municipal Government and Mr. Kangding, a director of the Public Concession Public Works Department, to take the Lijicha Lun from the Waibaidu Bridge to the Vanhuangdu, inspecting it section by section, following the map, and making detailed plans. Once decided, the relocation of ships along the river and the dismantling of the pier will be announced to facilitate construction. However, it is heard that although the dredging of Suzhou Creek this time is to facilitate transportation and develop commerce, the first to benefit are the public concessions. The matter of how to request the Public Works Department to subsidize the river dredging funds is currently being studied in detail.

Xu Kangfu's Concubine

Children Sue for Inheritance

Three Children as Plaintiffs

Concubine as Legal Representative

Claiming an Inheritance of 20,000 Yuan

Requesting Distribution According to Six Shares

After the death of Xu Kangfu, the former accountant of the General Chamber of Commerce, who died of illness the year before last, he left behind one wife and one concubine, and four children, who came to live separately. Now Xu Chen, Xu's concubine, with her six-year-old son Xu Yongnian, and fifteen-year-old daughter Xu Baolin, eleven-year-old daughter Xu Fulin, etc., as plaintiffs, the woman herself holding the position of legal representative, hired lawyer Yu Zhongluo to file a complaint with the Shanghai District Court, accusing the defendants Xu Shen (i.e., Xu Kangfu's first wife), Xu Yongchun, and mother and son of seizing the inheritance, requesting analysis according to six shares, etc. The terms are roughly: The plaintiff currently lives at No. 616, Jingxingli, North Henan Road. The agent is forty years old this year. Her husband Xu Kangfu served as the accountant of the General Chamber of Commerce for many years during his lifetime. After his death the year before last, the inheritance was very large and was taken away by the defendants. After mediation and negotiation by relatives and friends, the defendants were given a living allowance of 60 yuan per month, but after October of last year, the defendants stopped paying. All the inheritance, such as more than 9,000 yuan of shares in the Great World, more than 7,000 yuan of savings in the Lao Jiuzhang Silk Shop, more than 3,000 yuan of shares in the Commercial Press, and 600 yuan of savings in the Siming Bank, totaling more than 20,000 yuan, are requested to be distributed according to six shares, etc. The defendants Xu Shen and Xu Yongchun also hired lawyer Zhao Zuwei to file a defense, stating that the husband had taken Xu Chen as a concubine, living separately and cooking separately. The late husband lived in the concubine's residence for more than ten years. In the summer of the year before last, the husband died in the concubine's house, so the defenders transported the husband's remains back home to bury him and mourn him. Although there is a small amount of inheritance, it is not worth three or four thousand gold. The defenders repeatedly asked the agent to live together so that they could save money, but the agent refused all along, not knowing what the intention was, and should be refuted, etc. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Du opened a court hearing. Both parties arrived in court with lawyers. First, the plaintiff's agent Xu Chen pleaded the previous situation and requested analysis according to shares. The defendant Xu Chen said that she was 51 years old and from Shanghai. Xu Yongchun said that he was 22 years old and lived at No. 51, Shengshunli, Baoshan Road, Zhabei, and recounted the past. The questioner considered that the case was a family dispute and instructed the lawyers of both parties to reconcile it outside, with a deadline of three weeks. If there is no possibility of reconciliation, then a collective trial will be scheduled, and then the court will be adjourned.

Married Woman Uses

Criminal Litigation to Fight for Inheritance

Old Mother Is Already Seventy-Nine Years Old

Comes to Court with Daughter-In-Law and Grandchildren to Defend

Plaintiff's Purpose Is to Fight for Property

And Withdraws the Criminal Suit in Court

Recently, a woman Chen Wang and her mother Wang Lu, sister-in-law Wang Zeng, nieces Wang Fuzhen, Fuhua, Fumin, Fuying, Fuyong, etc., were involved in a lawsuit in the Special District Court for the inheritance of her late father Wang Yongchang. At the first trial yesterday, the entire family appeared in court. According to the plaintiff Chen Wang's complaint, after her father Yongchang passed away, the inheritance was managed by her mother Wang Lu and her brother Wang Baoshan. Her brother also died last year. He saw the content of the announcement published in the newspaper by Junyuan, which said that Wang Zeng had entrusted a lawyer to request Junyuan to grant her the right to manage her brother Baoshan's inheritance. She and Baoshan were children born to her late father. According to the current party program and the laws and regulations of the National Government, men and women are absolutely equal. Regardless of whether a woman is married or not, she has equal inheritance rights. She actually enjoys the same rights to the inheritance. How was the share book held by Wang Zeng drawn up, she never heard of it. However, she was arbitrarily disposing of the property that she should have obtained, which clearly constituted a crime under Article 356 of the Criminal Law, and requested that it be ordered to be re-analyzed on an average basis, etc. According to the defendant Wang Lu and others, in the defense complaint, Yongchang was a bookkeeper in the wooden line during his lifetime. The family was poor. He passed away on May 22, 23rd year of Guangxu (1897). His son Baoshan, first as a laborer, accumulated more than 20 years of hard work, with a little surplus of resources. Unfortunately, he died on October 19, 14th year of the Republic (1925), leaving behind only his wife Zeng (45 years old) and daughters Fuzhen (38 years old), Fuhua (26 years old), Fumin (24 years old), Fuying (23 years old), Fuyong (20 years old), etc. Later, because Fuzhen and others had grown up, each sought analysis. Although there was a dispute, they soon reconciled. Fuzhen and others then inherited their father's property, but the informant left the cabinet because of

Page 16

She was addicted to smoking and gambling, which led to the decline of her family. Her son Baoshan also provided financial assistance during his lifetime, and Fuzhen and others often provided relief. The informant was greedy and listened to rumors, misunderstanding the law that married women inherited property, intending to blackmail, and knowing that there was no reason to win, to avoid litigation costs and to harm others, so she filed a criminal prosecution. And this family property was entirely accumulated by Baoshan. How can the informant enjoy it? Her late husband Yongchang passed away in the 23rd year of Guangxu. Baoshan began to inherit at that time. At that time, unmarried women did not have the right to inherit property, let alone married women. (The interpretation of the Judicial Yuan on the 19th of November in the 18th year of the Republic (1929) on the law of inheritance rights of women's property, omitted.) And Baoshan died on October 19, 14th year of the Republic (1925). The original claim referred to last year, which was obviously false. Therefore, this petition requests to refute the plaintiff's lawsuit, etc. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Ge Zhitan opened a court. Except for Fuhua, Fumin, and Fuying, the remaining defendants arrived in court, among whom Wang Lu was 79 years old, with white hair fluttering. Three generations of grandparents and grandchildren came to court together, which was also a misfortune for the family. First, the plaintiff Chen Wang stated that her late father had an inheritance worth more than 300,000 yuan, which was first managed by her brother Baoshan. Her brother died in the 14th year of the Republic (1925). Her nieces Fuzhen and others had come to discuss the matter of analysis. At that time, she was promised a share, but later she was not allowed to know and was arbitrarily analyzed into eight shares. Her mother, sister-in-law, and Fuzhen's five sisters each got one share, and the remaining share was given to Fuzhen's son, and she got nothing, so she filed a lawsuit, etc. Judge Ge asked her whether she wanted to prosecute the defendants for criminal offenses because she had filed a criminal complaint. The woman replied, "My purpose is to seek a share of the property, and I do not hope that the defendants will be subject to criminal penalties." Judge Ge then briefly questioned the defendants who arrived in court and said to the plaintiffs and defendants, "This case is a lawsuit for analysis of inheritance. The plaintiff also stated in court that she did not want the defendants to be subject to criminal penalties. This case is completely a civil lawsuit and does not involve criminal matters." He also asked the plaintiff whether she could automatically request to withdraw from the case. At that time, Chen Wang also knew that she should not have filed a criminal prosecution. After hearing the order, she immediately declared that she was willing to withdraw the lawsuit. The court approved it. Thus, this three-generation property dispute criminal case came to an end.

Special District Court Trial

Brother-Killing Case Criminal

Police Investigation Confirmed

Sun Shibao Actually Killed His Brother

Family Forcibly Resisted During Arrest

Three People Charged with Obstructing Official Duties

Anhui native Sun Shibao, Sun Xia, and Sun Zhu were accused of murder. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu of the Special District Court held a trial. According to the police lawyer Ru Bao-yi, the defendant Sun Shibao killed his elder brother Sun Shilin with an axe on February 12th of this year at 5:45 AM. Sun Xia had two sons, Shilin (the elder) and Shibao (the younger). Zhu was the younger daughter-in-law, while the elder daughter-in-law was Wang. They all lived at No. 1753 Yinghua Lane, Robert Road.

Suspected Brother Had an Affair with Wife, Shibao was a carpenter, and Shilin was a steward on the Dehe Steamboat. Shilin returned home on January 26th of this year. On the evening of February 9th, Shilin asked his younger brother's wife, Sun Zhu, to bring the lamp upstairs. She looked for something upstairs for a while before coming downstairs with Shilin. At this time, Shibao returned home and saw his wife walking with his brother, immediately becoming suspicious. He argued with his wife that night.

Cries for Help Heard Upstairs On the night of the 11th, Shibao and his wife argued again. Shibao said to Zhu, "You've done a fine thing. I'll kill you both in the future to vent my anger." Shilin's wife overheard this. The next morning, the 12th, Sun Xia suddenly heard Shilin calling for help upstairs. She went upstairs with Wang and saw Shilin's head injured by an axe and on the verge of death. They reported to the Putuo Road Police Station, which sent detectives to investigate. Shilin was still able to speak but soon died.

Axe Still Had Blood Stains Afterwards, the police found the case quite bizarre and launched an investigation. When Shilin was murdered, only Sun Xia, Sun Shibao, Sun Wang, and Sun Pei's husband, Sun Chunqing, were at home. The police took these four to the police station for questioning and found a bloody axe in the stove room of the house. Therefore, they suspected that the crime was committed by someone in the family. However, due to lack of evidence, the four were temporarily released.

Bit Off Detective's Finger Shibao disappeared immediately after being released, which indicated that he was the murderer. The court issued a warrant for his arrest. Last night, they learned that Shibao had returned home and went to arrest him. When the detectives arrived at his home, Sun Xia and Sun Zhu came out to stop them and even bit the finger of detective Yao Changmin. Therefore, the two women were charged with obstructing official duties.

The Murderer Was Indeed Shibao According to the police investigation, the deceased and his wife had been estranged for five years and had not lived together. He also had many disagreements with his family. Therefore, Sun Xia deliberately concealed the truth. Because the family relied on Shibao for a living, they were afraid that their livelihood would be cut off if Shibao was arrested. However, the defendant still denied being Sun Shibao, claiming that his name was Xia Shaozeng and that Sun Xia was his aunt. Therefore, Sun Xia also denied that he was her son, and Sun Zhu even denied that he was her husband. But the police were certain that the defendant's name was Sun Shibao without any doubt.

Shibao Vigorously Denied A photo of Shibao found in Sun's house was presented as evidence to the defendant. He claimed that he was not Sun Shibao but Xia Shaozeng and that he, Shibao, and Shilin were cousins. Sun Zhu testified that her husband Shibao was dead. Judge Wu questioned Sun Xia briefly and ordered the defendants to be detained separately for another hearing at a later date.

6,000 Yuan Worth of Cloth

Robbed in the Huangpu River

The Incident Occurred on the 8th of this Month

The Case Was Only Solved the Day Before Yesterday

Thieves and Those Who Sold the Stolen Goods Were Arrested Together

The Original Stolen Goods Were Allowed to Be Returned to the Plaintiff First

New Prosperity, Yongfengli, and Yishunheng, three customs brokerage firms, hired a dock boat belonging to Fan Xiaohai and Song Changfa on the evening of the 8th of this month at 7:30 PM. They loaded nine boxes and one package of Zhigong wool, silk, and other fabrics, worth 6,000 yuan, at the Mitsubishi Company dock. They intended to transport them to the Longmao Warehouse dock in Pudong for transshipment onto the Zhaoxing Company's Lianxing Steamboat, preparing to transport them to other ports. When Fan's boat sailed through the Suzhou Creek estuary and returned to the center, a small boat sped over. Eight robbers were hidden in the boat. When they approached Fan's boat, the robbers jumped aboard. Two robbers took out handguns and tied up the two crew members, locking them in the cabin. Three robbers steered the boat to the Wuzhen Road Bridge on the Suzhou Creek and unloaded the nine boxes and one package of rejected goods, loading them onto a cargo truck and driving north. After the robbers left, the two tied-up crew members managed to loosen the ropes and go ashore, reporting the incident to the customs brokerage firms, who reported it to the Weituoma Road Water Police Station, requesting an investigation. The three customs brokerage firms offered a reward of 1,000 yuan to apprehend the robbers. Until the day before yesterday (the 23rd), at approximately 1:00 PM, the Water Police Station detectives Sun Agui, Wang Haiquan, Cheng Yongnian, Huang Zhenlin, etc., arrested the robbers Jiangbei native Ji Chunbao (also known as Ji Chunbao) and Pudong native Wan Jinbao on Aiduya Road and Ailaige Road in the French Concession, bringing them back to the police station. Wan confessed that the stolen goods were sold to Ruirong Silk Cocoon Store at No. 194 Wenge Situo Road in the Public Concession. The detectives reported this to Western Police Chief Kailiqiao, who, the next day, jointly with Huisi Police Station detective Xie Wanfang and Western detective from No. 118, searched the Ruirong Store and found three boxes of stolen goods, totaling 146 pieces. They arrested the store owner Gu Peiqing, a native of Shaoxing. Gu said that the pieces were introduced by Wan Zhongliang from Huzhou, who brought a person surnamed Zhao to store them. The detectives went to No. 171 Yuanda Store nearby and apprehended Wan, while Zhao escaped. Wan further confessed that Zhigong wool was mortgaged by him at Xu Bingji Silk Spinning Store at No. 362 Sheng'an Lane, Ningbo Road. The detectives went to the store, confiscated nine pieces of stolen Zhigong wool, and brought the store owner Xu Bingquan, a native of Shaoxing, to the Huisi Police Station for detention. Until yesterday morning, the Water Police and Huisi Police Stations sent the arrested Ji and Wan, the two robbers, and Gu, Wan, and Xu, the three who received the stolen goods, to the Special District Court, Second Criminal Court. Judge Wu Tingqi, along with Prosecutor Xu Meisheng, sat for the trial. The plaintiffs, New Prosperity Chang and the other two customs brokerage firms, hired lawyer Jiang Yiping to appear in court. Police lawyer Ru Bao-yi stated the case and requested a postponement to investigate and recover the remaining stolen goods. The Chinese and Western detectives reported the details of the case and presented the stolen goods as evidence. When questioned, the defendants Ji Chunbao and Wan Jinbao confessed that they were hired by Chen Changfa, who was still at large, to row the boat. Ji received a reward of 20 yuan, and Wan received 17 yuan. They did not know anything else. However, when the goods were unloaded, a person surnamed Zhao loaded the pieces onto a truck and transported them to the Ruirong Store. Wan Zhongliang had seen Changfa and others at the Asia Hotel. When questioned, Wan Zhongliang confessed that he lived with the person surnamed Zhao and introduced him to Xu Bingquan to mortgage the pieces because Zhao wanted to borrow 2,000 yuan. Xu Bingquan hired lawyer Liu Shichao to defend him, saying that Xu knew nothing about this matter. Gu Peiqing testified that he also knew nothing about it and that Wan had stored the goods secretly. Finally, plaintiff lawyer Jiang Yiping stated that all the confiscated stolen goods were currently in the police station's courtyard and that the weather was uncertain, fearing that the goods would be damaged by water. Therefore, he requested permission to return them first. After Judge Wu verified the confessions, he ordered Ji Chunbao, Wan Jinbao, and Wan Zhongliang to be taken back to the police station for detention. Xu Bingquan and Gu Peiqing each posted a bail of 2,000 yuan to await another hearing at a later date. All recovered stolen goods were allowed to be claimed by the plaintiff first.

U.S. Assessor's Office

Yesterday's Hearing of a Woman's Mental Illness Case

All Jurors Were Women

According to the Great Evening News, this morning (the 25th), the U.S. Assessor's Office held a trial for a mental illness case. All six jurors were women. The defendant was Mrs. Wegner, a German woman who had become an American citizen. She had been sent to China by a church in Philadelphia two years ago to preach in Hubei. Now, she was accused of having a mental illness, so the assessor's office held a trial. If she was indeed ill, she would be sent back to the United States. After the court opened at 9:30 AM, lawyer Li Ming represented the defendant, and prosecutor Sa Laide stated the case as usual. The nurses who cared for the defendant were called to testify. The court adjourned at 11:45 AM. The jurors went to the hospital to examine the defendant's condition and were scheduled to pronounce the verdict on Monday. According to reports, this was the first time a foreign court in China had women serve as jurors.

Municipal Health Bureau

Preventing Meningitis Epidemic

Injecting Workers with Preventive Vaccines

The Health Bureau, in view of the occurrence of cerebrospinal meningitis in neighboring areas, has provided assistance to prevent the disease and implemented various preventive methods in the city. Every day, personnel are sent to factories to inject workers with free cerebrospinal meningitis preventive vaccines. Since the implementation of free injections until April 15th, a total of 77 factories and organizations have been visited in one month, with 44,660 people receiving injections. The injections are intended to protect the health of workers and prevent the spread of cerebrospinal meningitis. However, the level of education of workers in various factories is uneven, and the number of people willing to be injected depends entirely on whether the factory supervisors are enthusiastic in persuading them. The number of factory supervisors who care about the health of workers and enthusiastically persuade them is still small. Therefore, the injections have not been popularized among workers. Some have never been injected, and some have only been injected once and not a second time. It can be seen that most factory supervisors have not been able to pay close attention to the protection of the health of workers. It is necessary for the administrative authorities to plan and supervise the methods further. The bureau plans to expand the scope of cholera preventive vaccine injections in the future and discuss joint promotions with the Municipal Party Committee, Social Bureau, and Public Security Bureau. Cerebrospinal meningitis in this city was originally only sporadic and not an epidemic. The bureau is now reporting that the number of cases in various hospitals has declined, so the free injections of cerebrospinal meningitis preventive vaccines will end at the end of April.

Appeal After the Banning of Superstitious Items

Since the Ministry of the Interior recently issued an order banning superstitious items such as tin foil, firecrackers, paper effigies, and funerary objects, the tin foil industry, the firecracker industry, and the paper effigy industry in this city are terrified of losing their livelihoods. The day before yesterday, they specially sent representatives Zhang Zhenfan, Wu Jian'an, and Wu Gengyun to request assistance from the Candle Industry to jointly make a broader appeal. The industry convened a meeting of the Smoke and Exchange Industry Association to discuss countermeasures. Mr. He Yinsheng expressed his opinion that Zhu Min, Director of the Zhejiang Provincial Government, is planning to submit a request to the National Government to order the ministry to modify the handling of the banning of superstitious items. It is hoped that the government will take into account the difficulties of the people and be able to obtain such modifications. As for the candle and incense industries, the association has separately submitted requests for clarification, stating that they are daily necessities, and it has been noted on record. Now that the tin foil industry, etc., has requested cooperation, the industry will, when necessary, make a legitimate appeal based on the principle of people's livelihood. It is said that the smoke and exchange industry attaches great importance to this matter. Because of the reorganization, an announcement will be made as soon as it is completed.

Former Provisional Court Documents

Permission to Exchange for Ministry-Issued Documents

Deadline is the End of April

After the establishment of the Special District High and District Courts, the deadline for the use of various documents sold by the former Provisional Court and the Court of Appeal was limited to April 10th. An announcement had been made. However, the lawyers in this city had purchased and stored many of these documents. If those that had not been used by April 10th were to be discarded, it would be too uneconomical. Xu Weizhen, President of the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, and Wang Zhennan, Chief Prosecutor, specially telegraphed the Ministry of Judicial Administration, requesting a modification of the measures. An order has been issued approving an extension until the 30th of this month. Xu and Wang jointly announced yesterday, announcing the permission to exchange for Ministry-issued documents. The Ministry of Judicial Administration's telegram states, "The office is aware of your telegram. Lawyers and litigants who have purchased and stored various temporary documents sold by the former Shanghai Public Concession Provisional Court and the Court of Appeal will be allowed to have the Shanghai Lawyers Association exchange them for Ministry-issued documents from your branch court before April 30th of this year. They will be void after the deadline. Immediately announce this to the public. The exchange of the documents from the former Provisional Court should be reported for special reimbursement and must be observed." Therefore, we hereby announce this to the public.

A Thief in Western Suit Trespassed the Wall to Steal

The Japanese Man Cursed Unceasingly

At approximately 3:00 AM yesterday morning, at the home of a Westerner at No. 153 Bei Shanzhong Road in the French Concession, a thief dressed in a Western suit was about to climb over the wall to steal when he was spotted by the Westerner. A Hooligan Was "Planted with Lotus Flowers"

Yong native Ding Amao, 25 years old, lived at No. 9 Chengda Lane, Old Garbage Bridge. He used to be in the steamboat business but has now become a hooligan, making a living by extortion. 195 Cases of Explosives

Detained for Lack of Passport

Qian Zuomin, patrol captain of the Wusong Fourth Detachment of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol, inspected two suspicious wharf boats near Donggou, Pudong, the day before yesterday. They found as many as 195 cases of explosives in the cabin. Zhu Hesheng, an Anhui native who was escorting the explosives, was arrested. The seized evidence was taken to the detachment. After a brief interrogation by the patrol officer, it was transferred to the South City Brigade. During the preliminary trial by Captain Xu, Zhu, 21 years old, confessed that the explosives, totaling 195 cases, were hired by the wharf to load two boats and ordered him to escort them to Pingqiao, Hangzhou, to be used for blasting mountains. The captain believed that since he was transporting a large number of explosives without a passport, he was undoubtedly a smuggler. He ordered a report to be submitted to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Interesting Incident in a Divorce Case

Old Sisters Quarrel Violently

A Bag of Feces as a Prank

Guan Zhao, a 55-year-old woman from Yancheng, lived in Qingyan Zuo Alley in the South City. She had a daughter named Lin Di, 25 years old this year, who was fairly attractive. In the sixteenth year of the Republic of China (1927), she was betrothed through a matchmaker to Yin Quan, the son of Shen He'gao, the brother-in-law of Zhao, who lived at No. 21 Shide Lane, Youche Wharf. They had been married for three years. However, after Lin Di married into the family, she was always displeased because her husband was deaf and lacked a proper business. Therefore, there were constant quarrels between the couple, and the sound of criticism reached outside the house. Fearing that they would not be able to grow old together in this situation, she filed a complaint with the Shanghai District Court a few days ago, requesting a divorce. Yesterday, after the court ordered the defendant Shen He'gao and others to appear, Zhao, Shen's wife, received the summons. She assumed that her sister Guan Zhao had instigated the action. Filled with anger, she immediately resorted to a prank. She secretly prepared a bag of feces and rushed to her sister's house at 5:30 PM yesterday afternoon. At first, she made a serious protest, but when they disagreed, a conflict broke out. Guan Zhao was weak and unable to resist, falling to the ground. Shen Zhao immediately poured the feces she had prepared into her mouth, causing Guan Zhao's face, neck, and other parts of her body to be covered in filth, with an unbearable stench. Guan Zhao, at this point, was also filled with uncontrollable anger. She used all her strength to prop herself up and managed to grab her sister Shen Zhao, going to the first sub-station of the first district to file a complaint for investigation. The director ordered them to be detained temporarily for preliminary review.

Why Commit Suicide Because of Illness?

Zhou Qintao Rescued After Jumping into the Huangpu River

The Longmao Steamboat Company's ferryboat, running between Wuma Road in Puxi and Longmao Wharf in Lujiazui, Pudong, was returning to Pudong from Shanghai at 7:00 AM yesterday. Just as it arrived in the center of the river, near the bow of a British warship, a young passenger jumped into the Huangpu River to commit suicide. Fortunately, he was rescued by British sailors on the warship's small motorboat. Xia Abao, the steamboat's captain, sent him to the Water Police Station. According to the young man's confession, his name was Zhou Qintao, 21 years old, from Guangdong. Because he suffered from headaches and the treatment was ineffective, he became tired of life and jumped into the river to end his life. He had a friend in Shanghai named Zhou Fugen, who was a tea server at the Zhonghua Fengji Flour Company at No. 50 Tianzhutang Street. According to the confession, the police chief advised him, "It is common for an illness to not heal immediately. Why are you so short-sighted and seek death because of illness? The best course of action now is to go home and seek medical treatment." After finishing his admonishment, he ordered the detectives to summon his friend to take him away.

Recent News on the Meiya Silk Factory Strike

The Second Factory Has Resumed Work

The Meiya Silk Factory workers, on the grounds that the management did not fulfill the agreed-upon conditions, jointly went on strike with the First, Second, Third, Fourth, Fifth, Sixth, and Eighth branches. The details have already been reported in various newspapers. It is now reported that the Municipal Social Bureau, together with the Municipal Party Committee's People's Training Committee, issued a notice ordering a return to work. The Second Factory complied with the order and resumed work on the morning of April 22nd. The remaining factories have delayed their return to work and are said to be handled separately. Detailed explanations and instructions have been given regarding the workers' requests, and they should be followed. The following is an excerpt from the original text: (A) Regarding the factory's violation of the conditions agreed upon by labor and management, (1) Regarding the refusal of standing committee members of the labor union, the factory must not refuse representatives of the labor union that has been approved and registered by the government. (2) Regarding the extension of working hours and the signing of temporary worker contracts, if the factory needs all workers to extend their working hours beyond 10.5 hours, it must first obtain the consent of the labor union and then post a notice. If the factory posts a notice unilaterally without the consent of the labor union, workers who do not come to the factory to work will not be considered absent. The contract format for temporary workers must first be submitted to the bureau for approval. When necessary, it can be signed temporarily by the factory and the temporary workers. (3) Regarding the failure of miscellaneous apprentices to increase their wages after six months of work, the factory should provide a daily allowance of four yuan. (4) Regarding the failure to issue merit and demerit bonuses as in 1927, the rules for merit and demerit should be submitted by both labor and management, stating the reasons, and submitted to the bureau for approval. (5) Regarding national holidays promulgated by the National Government, where no rest or wages are given, the orders of the National Government should be followed. (6) Regarding workers injured at the factory due to work or suffering a sudden illness during work hours, the factory is not responsible for medical expenses or wages, the factory should follow the provisions of Article 7 of the labor-management agreement. (7) Regarding the failure of the gatekeepers to promptly notify workers when their relatives and friends come to the factory to visit for important matters, the labor side should follow the provisions of Article 15 of the factory rules and regulations, but the gatekeepers must not deliberately make things difficult. (B) Regarding the conditions imposed by the factory, 1. Regarding apprentices and miscellaneous apprentices who are promoted to formal workers upon completion of their apprenticeship, and the issuance of fixed-term employment contracts to old workers, old workers may be exempted from signing employment contracts. Apprentices promoted to formal workers upon completion of their apprenticeship and newly hired workers must sign employment contracts. 2. Regarding workers' savings, which cannot be withdrawn for urgent matters, the factory should submit the savings regulations to the bureau for approval before proceeding. 3. Regarding workers who accidentally damage raw materials or finished products due to mechanical failure, the factory should force compensation, both labor and management should follow the provisions of Article 19 of the factory rules and regulations. 4. Regarding the factory's practice of providing uniforms to workers who arrive at the factory on time at the start of work, which is now abolished, if the factory has this practice, it should continue to follow the practice. (C) Regarding the request for the factory to fulfill the agreed-upon conditions, 1. Regarding the request for the factory to abide by the conditions agreed upon by both parties in 1927, both labor and management should abide by these conditions. 2. Regarding the request for the factory to immediately abolish the harsh conditions, each condition has been explained. 3. Regarding the change from jacquard looms to plain looms, if a weaver resigns, the loom must still be assigned to a jacquard loom apprentice and not to an apprentice from another department, this request conflicts with the factory's administrative power and workers must not interfere. 4. Regarding the working hours for miscellaneous workers during each holiday, if the leave is less than one-quarter of a day, it should not be considered leave and the wage increase should not be deducted, this request conflicts with Article 5 of the labor-management agreement for the industry (workers who do not stop working within half a month will receive a wage increase for one day) and should not be discussed. The above explanations have also been instructed to the factory for compliance. The disputes may be resolved soon.

Free Talk

Smile It Away - Haike 海客

A: I am most afraid of hearing the horn of a car in my life. Every time I hear it, I am frightened.

B: Why?

A: Because my chauffeur stole my car. Along with it, he also stole my tigress-like wife. For the past year, it has been a great relief. But whenever I hear a horn, I am afraid he will send her back. So I cannot help but be frightened.

A: I once had a very good police dog. It showed welcome to gentlemen. And would bite rascals.

B: Where is that dog now? Maybe I can take a look?

A: I have given him away to someone. Because he was biting me all the time.

A: Nearly half of the male employees in my company are in love with my female secretary.

B: Doesn't that hinder their jobs?

A: Not really. It's just that they all want to be promoted and get a raise, to win her heart. Therefore, they are working harder.

A: On your engagement ring. Is your fiancée's name engraved?

B: Yes. But I had the craftsman engrave it particularly shallowly. So that I can erase it later and engrave another girl's name.
