Social News

Customs of the Indigenous People of Borneo

On the wave-swept shores of Borneo live several savage tribes. These tribes, even now, remain in a primitive state, living with wild beasts in the deep mountains, almost isolated from the modern world. They live in simple shelters, moving every year with the changing farms. They wear very little, using only a piece of bark more than a丈 long to wrap tightly around their lower bodies. However, the women wear a little more. As for food, besides hunted mountain birds and beasts and fish, they eat leaves that grow year-round. Because the land is very rich and their desires are not high, they can live every day without worry. This is probably the reason why they do not progress. Speaking of their customs, they are even more covered with a very rich primitive color. All kinds of things not easily seen and heard in the world are still preserved in their folklore. Now I will describe a few of the more interesting ones to get a glimpse of the general nature of their customs.

Listening to Bird Sounds

Among the local indigenous people, there is a very strange custom of listening to bird sounds. Whenever they go out, whether on land or water, they pay very close attention to the sounds of birds. From the melodious chirping, they can distinguish the good or bad fortune of the trip. This superstition has a very deep impact on their minds. Therefore, if they hear unfavorable bird sounds on the way, they would rather abandon all their efforts and turn back home. From this phenomenon, we can think of their worship of birds.

However, the bird sounds they listen to are not indiscriminate, nor are they listened to randomly. For example, the direction of the bird's call, the pitch of the call, all of these are related. If I were to explain this in detail, it would be very interesting, but unfortunately, I am not very familiar with it, so I will have to leave it out for now.

Because they worship birds, they have a feeling of not daring to harm birds. If, at any time, a bird they worship flies to the treetops in front of or behind their house and chirps all day and night, they become uneasy and rush to take some cakes and fruits to the tree to offer and pray. They believe that by doing this, they can not only avoid the arrival of disaster but also gain good fortune.

Their custom of listening to bird sounds, I think, is nothing more than that caused by the kind of heart that worships nature.

Poison Fish Festival

Every year in June and July, the weather is very dry, and the water in the river gradually recedes. At this time, they have the Poison Fish Festival. Before the festival, the nearby residents share the responsibility of collecting fish vines. The so-called fish vine is a kind of vine plant that contains poison. Extracting its juice can make fish dizzy and float to the surface as if dead, allowing people to seize them. When this kind of fish vine is collected to a considerable extent, and the river water has receded very shallowly, they jointly decide on a date. Once the date is set, everyone is almost joyful, hoping that day will come soon. In this atmosphere of joy, they must also busy themselves preparing various spears. Those who are more particular will paint the ends of the spear shafts with various colors, or tie a few small bells, so that they ring when thrown. In addition, they have to spend several days working to fence off the shallower parts of the river with wooden stakes, with a large cage placed in the middle. This is to prevent the fish from swimming underwater after eating the fish vine.

On the day of the festival, no matter how far away people live, they row medium-sized boats with three or four people in each boat towards the place where the festival is held. Usually, people from far away arrive the day before and spend the night on the sandbar. The next day, when the morning light is faint, everyone prepares to set off, laughing and talking, a kind of ecstasy inspiring everyone's hearts. Once the order to set off is given, everyone throws the fish vine water into the river together and then traces downstream. At this time, everyone holds a spear in their right hand, waiting for the fish to float to the surface. Therefore, speaking of how many fish are caught, half depends on chance and half depends on the technique of throwing. They hunt like this until dusk, and then they return home, slightly satisfied with the few fish they have speared.

Collecting Ancient Jars

They are born with a fondness for ancient jars, so once they have savings, they try to buy ancient jars. The value of an ancient jar is about ten yuan for cheap ones, but as high as several thousand yuan for expensive ones. People who collect ancient jars are always wealthy and powerful, such as the village leaders.

These people who collect ancient jars seem to have the vanity of flaunting their status. For example, whenever there is a banquet, they decorate the ancient jars they treasure with red cloth and display them at the banquet for guests to appreciate. On the part of the host, they naturally feel a rare sense of pride, and on the part of the guests, they naturally cannot avoid admiring and envying them.

Economic Circles of Various Countries Transitioning from Prosperity to Decline

Increased Ship Layups in Britain Hit Particularly Hard

Recently, the shipping industry in various countries has been sluggish, with ships being laid up one after another. Britain, known as a maritime nation, has been hit the hardest. According to news from a certain source, the number of ships laid up in the main commercial ports of mainland Britain (now Ireland) is as follows:

Total　British Ships over 1,000 Tons

January 1, 1929　3.971　279　326

October 11　385　997　246.24

January 1, 1930　352,699　327,387

That is, on January 1 of this year, there was an increase of 22,888 tons (6.94%) compared to January 1 of last year, and an increase of 86,622 tons (32.58%) compared to October 1 of last year. This is particularly evident for ships over 1,000 tons, with an increase of approximately 81,100 tons (approximately 33%) compared to October 1 of last year, and an increase of 48,061 tons (17.21%) compared to January 1 of last year. The reason is that the harvest of wheat, a major commodity, has been greatly reduced in the world's major producing areas this period, and the surplus capacity for export is low. At the same time, the cultivation in Europe, a region in need, is still not bad, leading to a gradual decrease in shipments. In addition, corn from Argentina and other countries has not yet reached the shipping season. Moreover, the economic circles of various countries have transitioned from the prosperity of one or two years ago to a reactive state of decline. Due to the sluggish shipping market and low freight rates, shipowners have no choice but to lay up ships.

Malay Drama YS

(Malay Drama is Much Better Than Chinese Drama) No one would believe that the drama of the foolish Malay people, who have no culture at all, would receive such praise from the audience, unless you have been to Southeast Asia and seen Malay drama.

The Malay people's talent for music and dance can be said to be a gift from heaven. It is said that their drama originated in India, but they were able to assimilate Indian drama and create a Malay drama, which is very admirable.

The material for Malay drama is also mostly taken from Indian folk tales and stories. Tragic plots are more common. We can also say that nine out of ten Malay dramas are (tragic dramas). This kind of (tragic drama) is naturally not very suitable for the trend of the times. However, we can appreciate it as a literary work. In addition, the plot is often interspersed with moving love songs, and the music is purely taken from Western instruments. The melodious and moving singing is truly rare. Therefore, we can also see the Malay people's skill in using and improving things.

The actors in Malay drama include both men and women. Men play male roles, and women play female roles, unlike our country, where men can play female roles, and women can play male roles. The effort put into expressions and acting is very satisfactory. As for the stage setting, they strive for realism. Even a flower or a blade of grass must be lifelike before they are let go. I wonder what the Chinese drama circles think of this spirit of theirs.

Finally, I also hope that the Chinese drama circles will work hard so that the audience of overseas Chinese will cancel the phrase "(Malay drama is much better than Chinese drama)."

Malay Sorcery by Shi. Duo.

The word "sorcery" is commonly used by our compatriots and means "secret medicine." Speaking of Malay secret medicine, its harm is truly unimaginable. Often, without realizing it, it can make your limbs or a certain part of your body crippled or even take your life. Moreover, when performing this kind of secret medicine, it is so mysterious and skillful that it is difficult to catch and prevent, so the compatriots who interact with them are very afraid of offending them in any way, fearing that they will play the trick of sorcery. Because the Malay people are a nation that has not yet shed its savage state, their minds are very narrow, and the thought of revenge is easily stirred up in their chests. So once you have offended them, they will bear a grudge and seek revenge when the opportunity arises.

They not only use this sorcery to seek revenge, but also use it to seek love or protect fruit trees. For example, if they are attracted to a certain girl but cannot win her favor due to various reasons, they use sorcery, either smearing oil on her flesh or drawing symbols for her to step over. Once the girl is affected by the sorcery, she will become infatuated with the man, no longer having the previous attitude of refusal. How mysterious and strange this is! As for using it to protect fruit trees, it is even more interesting. For example, if there is an orchard full of fruit and they are afraid that people will steal it, they hide this secret medicine at the base of the fruit trees, so that anyone who touches the base of the tree cannot move away or will not have good results when they return home.

Because sorcery has many uses, speaking of its types, there are also many kinds, and the raw materials for making this poison also vary depending on the type. For example, poisonous grasses and trees in the mountains, the pulp of fruits, and the marrow of animals are all materials for preparing sorcery. It is said that the most famous and fierce of the poisons is the juice of a poisonous tree called Iplb Batang. To extract it, they dig a hole in the tree, use a bamboo tube to collect the juice that flows out, and then mix it with the pulp of a certain grass root and boil it together. This evaporates the water and forms a solid, which can then be used.

Both plays have recently been rehearsed thoroughly and are expected to be a great success.

Art World

Introduction to the Study of Oil Painting

Chen Baoyi

A few months ago, I saw the book (The Study of Oil Painting). This book is a collection of 40 lectures by 25 famous artists, selected from the articles solicited and published by the Japanese art magazine AIRLIER over the years. After reading it, I felt that this book is quite suitable for young people studying Western painting to refer to, because these dozens of short articles all describe the key points of research and production. Some describe the experience of production, some explain the methods of using materials, and some can give us a new hint in the research process. Especially considering the position of Easterners studying oil painting, it is enough to make us realize the path we should take. Therefore, I think this book is a very appropriate compass for our Eastern researchers. I then engaged in translation and writing in my spare time and am now nearing completion. I think I may have the opportunity to compile it into a book sometime.

Most of the original authors are contemporary leaders in the Japanese Western painting world, such as Yamamoto Kanae, Umehara Ryuzaburo, Nakagawa Kigen, Yorozu Tetsugoro (deceased), Okumura Hiroshi, Nakagawa Kazumasa, Hayashi Yoshie, Nabei Katsuyuki (and others omitted). Each article contains the unique characteristics of the author, that is, the painter. Therefore, when I translated, I felt that if I arbitrarily changed the words and expressions of the original author for the sake of habitual reading, so that the reader could not feel the spirit of the original text, it would be contrary to the translator's wishes and would be unfair to the original author. Therefore, although I feel my own clumsiness, I still try to convey the original text. Therefore, perhaps some sentences in it will seem difficult to understand to the reader. However, I feel that it seems unavoidable due to the reasons mentioned above, so I especially ask the reader for forgiveness.

It is also like what the preface of the original book said (as for what kind of golden words will be discovered from this book and how to apply them, this is the scope of research for the readers). Also, the translator has added annotations to various specialized terms and more difficult points in the original text. Taking advantage of the current opportunity, I will first select and publish a few of the translated drafts here. Also, I plan to publish the sister book (The Study of Sketching) in sequence.

April 1930, Translator's Note

Nakagawa Kigen's Solo Exhibition Opens

Japanese painter Nakagawa Kigen is currently traveling in China, carrying many works. The Shanghai Japanese Rainbow Society has scheduled a solo exhibition for Nakagawa on the 26th and 27th of this month at the Japanese Club in Hongkou. All are welcome to visit.

Babini Man Ru

Modern Italian Writer

Giovanni Papini, the Italian writer whose (Storio id Cristo) caused a sensation in Europe and America, has once again attracted the world's attention with the sudden publication of his (Sand Agostino). Taking advantage of this opportunity, it seems appropriate to briefly introduce this Italian literary giant, who is not very familiar to us.

In 1906, Papini began his writing career with his collection of short stories Tragico Quotidiano and his collection of essays II Crepuscolo die Filosofi. 1906 was a very important year. The old Carducci Ottocentismo had split. Croce had come to the fore, and Marinetti and Futurism were on the horizon. In philosophy, empiricism had suffered a significant defeat, and the introduction of new foreign theories had a great influence. William James' pragmatism was one of them, but Bergson's philosophy did not make much progress in this peninsula. This phenomenon can be said to represent the significant difference between southern and northern Europe in thought today. In fact, James's theory was merged with the poetic and heroic characteristics of modern Italy, producing a new idealism of the nineteenth century. Our man Papini, who sees himself as a "creator" (Dewiurge), made his debut at this time, which was truly opportune.

However, it would not be entirely correct to say that Papini's literary career began when his works were first published in 1906. Accurately speaking, his literary career began three years earlier, when he founded and presided over the argumentative, pragmatic journal II Leonardo. This was one of the characteristics of the Florentine Renaissance in the early 20th century. This publication was a typical Tuscan mouthpiece, but it ran for five years from 1903 to 1907.

Page 26

In 1908, La Voce was founded, and Papini later became the editor of this publication. In these two publications, Papini the critic gradually evolved. This was a (self-critical) critic, a judge of works of art and their shortcomings. His fierce momentum gave his style an inelegant state and personality expression. As for his style, it was then markedly deliberately crude and barbaric, as well as ambiguous phrases of the Neo-Romantics and Futurists. However, from this chaotic style, there would later emerge a critic who spoke with (sincere rhetoric) and concealed his sincerity with arrogant humility. Later, around 1910, a collapse occurred. Papini went through a mental crisis, at which time thought, life, and art all seemed to disappoint him greatly. His previous idealism had been completely shattered. His tragedy was the tragedy of a strong-willed man. He had explored the greatest possibilities of the will. He had discovered that besides this, there was only "death, madness, or the monastery." His first instinctive move was to escape. He wanted to create an external value, a value outside of the self. As a result, we saw his L'altra Meta. In this book, he tried to establish a philosophy of negation and contradiction, but he did not succeed much. This can be clearly seen in his autobiography Un Uomo Finito, published in the same year.

This period continued for some time. The years before the war were Papini's most painful years. The old Voce, the mouthpiece of literary, political, and philosophical thought, whose writers included many writers and philosophers, died in 1914, on the eve of the war. In the same year, although Papini and Soffici founded L'acerbe, this publication was also taken away by the war in 1915. However, although these two publications have passed away, Papini has made indelible contributions in their pages. He laid the foundation for national culture, spread a new intellectual atmosphere, overthrew old ideas, and ignited new thoughts. However, the sentiment of hatred did not diminish because of this, and remained the main sentiment in his articles.

From all of this, a better poet emerged. After the great storm passed, he discovered that he had many things in common with those heroic, reckless young people. Perhaps this was because of the war, but in the midst of all the devastation after the war, Papini was still Papini. His personality did not disappear at all, and he was still the same character as before.

After the war, Papini became famous throughout the world for his biographical works. For Papini, the meaning of biography is poetry. He used to say that the subject matter of biography should be a kind of ("intellectual thing"). This statement now seems quite doubtful. In fact, what he is concerned about is ("that living and complete reality, that is, individuality"). He himself is a person with the strongest individuality, so he regards individuality as the most important thing. He looks at history from the perspective of autobiography, and looks at the whole picture of society from the perspective of individual character. He tells us that the great figures of the past are all fragments of history. From these fragments, we can find ourselves. They are also corpses. We must breathe the breath of our lives into these corpses.

After reading his (Augustine), we believe that this is true. From Saint Augustine, that ("fragment of history"), did Papini not find himself? To Saint Augustine, that ("corpse") of the past, did Papini not breathe the breath of his life into him, making him a living person with a soul? The success of Papini's biographical works is mostly due to those two sentences.

Thomas Mann's Novella Masterpiece

Premature Grief Man Ru

A Representation of the Disillusioned State of Germany After the War

Everything Thomas Mann writes always receives a respectful and enthusiastic welcome in Germany. Therefore, when this long (short story) was published three years ago, although it was not as good as his novella masterpiece (Death in Venice) (Der Tod in Venedig), it was still very well received. However, foreigners who read this novel may not find it as intimate and interesting as Germans, because it contains a special kind of sentimental emotion, expressing the general disillusioned psychology of Germany after the war. It sadly writes about the family life and daily emotions of the dilapidated and impoverished German professional class and intellectual class in the years since the Great War. This situation is written very realistically, and still feels real when we hear it now, but the depressed and melancholic psychology and atmosphere that permeates the book cannot be appreciated unless one has had this kind of experience oneself. Therefore, foreign readers will not get a strong interest from this novel. However, if we want to know the general psychology and ordinary life of Germany after the war, then this novel is a very appropriate book. (English translation titled Early Sorrow, published by Martin Secker, London, priced at five shillings)

The structure of this novel is very thin, and the events that occur in it are very small. Roughly, it is like this: There is a history professor, Cornelius, who has two sons, Bertolt and Ingrid. These two young men hold a party at home to entertain their friends. They are all uninhibited and extremely disillusioned young people. They feel very sensitive, but their emotions are very cold. His stubborn character was created and hardened by the Great War. They all have a sense of the shortness of life and the disappearance of youth. They all hold the idea of seizing the day. Their mood is the same as that of most young people. For example, among their full house of friends, a large part of them have the same thoughts. Suppose that one of them, a very ordinary young man, danced several times with their little sister, the professor's beloved daughter, Erna. He had fun with her, talked about love, and teased her. For him, it was just acting on the spur of the moment, so he soon forgot about this little girl and forgot about this matter. However, that little girl seemed very precocious and was greatly provoked. Therefore, she felt very sad about his later indifference and cried. The adults saw that this little child suddenly cried, and did not know why. Of course, they used the old method of dealing with children and sent her to bed. But she was still crying, and no matter how they comforted her, they could not comfort her, especially her father's comfort made her feel especially sad. The old professor felt inexplicable and could not figure out the reason for his beloved daughter's strange sorrow. Later, the young man who caused the trouble knew about this matter, guessed the reason, and went to Erna's bedroom to kiss her, comfort her, and stay with her by the bed until she fell asleep. This was the first time Erna tasted the sorrow of life, but she tasted it too early.

The main body of the story is roughly like this. The plot is certainly very simple, but the book is full of profound thoughts, so it is definitely not a superficial and empty work. In this novel, we see the psychology of the old professor, who represents the father's generation, although it does not conflict with the psychology of the young people of the son's generation, it is always inconsistent. On the one hand, he prepares the arrangements for his children's party, but on the other hand, he thinks about what meaning this party has for him, a history professor. His heart belongs to that ("orderly and disciplined historical past"). The current excessive indulgence is not harmonious for him. He feels

that the past is immortal, that is to say, the past is dead, and death is the root of all sacredness and all lasting meaning.

Everything in the past is past, but everything in the present is very different from the past. The psychology of young people and the psychology of old people are very far apart, but old people do not have to resist the ("present"). ("The present") is the territory of young people, and the world of ("the past") is the world of old people, although it has passed, however, ("the past is immortal,") this is the psychology of old people.

Literary Anecdotes

New Winner of the Goncourt Literary Prize

The Goncourt Literary Prize, which is considered the most important of the various prizes in France, was awarded last year to the novelist Arland (Marcel Arland) for his novel (Order) (L'ordre). Arland is only thirty years old this year. His first work (Foreign Lands) (Terres Etrangeres) was published in 1923, followed by several novels in succession. (Order) was published last year and consists of three large volumes. It is a study of post-war France. (Ming)

Barbusse as Editor-in-Chief

Barbusse (Henry Barbusse), the author of (Under Fire) and (Clarity), is now the editor-in-chief of a newspaper in Paris. There are some great celebrities in his editorial department. Dr. A. Einstein, the inventor of the theory of relativity, is also one of them. (Ming)

New Works by German Historical Novelists

Walter Von Molo, who has gained a lofty status in Germany for several historical novels, has recently published a modern romance novel entitled Dis Scheidung. This novel examines the issue of marriage and divorce from a man's point of view. It interestingly describes a modern marriage and the reactionary conflicts of the main characters, etc. (Ming)

O'Flaherty Has Another New Book

O'Flaherty (Liam O Flaberty), the most important young novelist in Ireland, produces a lot and quickly. It is said that he will publish another novel this spring. This novel is based on his experiences at the front during the European War and is strangely titled (The Return of the Brute). O'Flaherty served as a foot soldier in the Irish Guards and was wounded in Belgium in 1917. (Ming)

New Book Club in Spain

There are now many ("new book clubs") in the United States, with members ranging from 40,000 to 100,000. The so-called ("new book club") is that each month the editorial department of the club selects the best of the newly published books and distributes them to each member (of course, they have to pay). This kind of group has a lot of authority in the United States. Now there is also one in the UK, but it is not very developed, because the British are more old-fashioned and there are many people who do not agree with this method. Recently, I heard that there is also a ("Spanish New Book Club") in Madrid, and the method is the same as that of the UK and the US. The most recently selected book is a translated novel called Pobre Blanco, which translated into English is Poor White. It was originally an old work by Sherwood Anderson. Now, in order to return the favor, Viping Press, the American publisher that publishes the original book, has also translated and printed a Spanish masterpiece, Zamacois's (Roots) (Roots). (Ming)
